        <div class="container">
            <!-- START ARTICLE FEED -->
            <section class="articles">
                <div class="column is-12 is-offset-0">
                    <!-- START ARTICLE -->
                    <div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://addshore.com/2021/11/mwcli-ci-in-wikimedia-gitlab-docker-in-docker/?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=mwcli-ci-in-wikimedia-gitlab-docker-in-docker"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">mwcli CI di Wikimedia GitLab ( buruh pelabuhan di buruh pelabuhan )</font></font></a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">22:11, Senin, 01 November 2021 UTC</font></font></span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p><a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Cli" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">mwcli</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> adalah alat CLI golang yang telah saya kerjakan selama setahun terakhir untuk menggantikan </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">lingkungan pengembangan </font></font><a href="https://github.com/addshore/mediawiki-docker-dev" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">mediawiki-docker-dev</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> yang tidak sengaja saya buat beberapa tahun yang lalu (antara lain). </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Saya tidak memulai CLI, tetapi saya melakukan fungsi seperti mediawiki-docker-dev ini.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Saat beberapa titik melalui perjalanan pengembangan, menjadi jelas bahwa salah satu cara untuk membedakan lingkungan baru dan lama adalah melalui beberapa CI dan pengujian yang ketat.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Ini dimulai dengan CI yang berjalan pada </font></font><a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Continuous_integration/Qemu" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">node Qemu</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> sebagai bagian dari infrastruktur CI Wikimedia Jenkins bersama yang terhubung ke Gerrit, tempat kode dikembangkan. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Ini akhirnya menjadi sangat lambat, dan melibatkan banyak langkah manual.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Iterasi berikutnya melihat sebagian besar pengembangan terjadi di
 </font></font><a href="https://github.com/addshore/addshore-mwcli" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">garpu saya sendiri di Github</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , memanfaatkan Tindakan Github. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Perubahan kemudian akan disalin ke Gerrit untuk tinjauan akhir setelah tes CI berjalan.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dan akhirnya repositori dipindahkan ke </font></font><a href="https://gitlab.wikimedia.org/releng/cli" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">instance GitLab Wikimedia</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> baru </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">(sedang dalam proses), di mana saya dapat menggunakan GitLab Runners yang diberdayakan oleh mesin di </font></font><a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Portal:Cloud_VPS" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Wikimedia Cloud VPS</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> .</font></font></p>
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large img-responsive"><img alt="" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a3/Gitlab_Pipelines_Screenshot_-_releng-mwcli_2021.png" class=" img-responsive">
<figcaption><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Tangkapan layar pipeline GitLab beraksi untuk proyek mwcli</font></font></figcaption>
</figure>
<span id="more-7904"></span>
<h2><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Gambaran</font></font></h2>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Saya memiliki proyek Cloud VPS khusus untuk mesin yang digunakan sebagai runner untuk proyek </font></font><a href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/T294283" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">mwcli</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ( </font><a href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/T294283" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">T294283</font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ). </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Saat ini 2 runner dikonfigurasi, masing-masing dengan 4 core, memori 8GB, dan disk 20GB yang menjalankan debian buster.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Pelari menggunakan Docker di buruh pelabuhan, yang merupakan salah satu cara terdokumentasi untuk menggunakan pelaksana buruh pelabuhan </font></font><a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/runner/executors/docker.html#use-docker-in-docker-with-privileged-mode" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">per dokumentasi GitLab</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> . </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Saya belum melakukan tinjauan lengkap tentang kemungkinan implikasi keamanan dari pendekatan ini, dan perlu dicatat bahwa mesin virtual hanya menjalankan CI untuk 1 proyek ini, dan hanya anggota proyek yang memiliki kemampuan untuk menjalankan CI.</font></font></p>
<h2><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Instalasi</font></font></h2>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Anda perlu menginstal buruh pelabuhan. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Anda dapat mengikuti </font></font><a href="https://docs.docker.com/get-docker/" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">panduan pemasangan buruh pelabuhan</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , atau melakukan sesuatu seperti ini…</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-php">sudo apt-get update sudo
apt-get remove docker docker-engine docker.io containerd runc sudo
apt-get install \ apt-transport-https \ ca-certificates \ curl \
gnupg \ lsb-release curl -fsSL https:<span class="hljs-comment">//download.docker.com/linux/debian/gpg | sudo gpg
--dearmor -o /usr/share/keyrings/docker-archive-keyring.gpg</span>
<span class="hljs-keyword">echo</span> \ <span class="hljs-string">"deb [arch=amd64
signed-by=/usr/share/keyrings/docker-archive-keyring.gpg]
https://download.docker.com/linux/debian \ $(lsb_release -cs)
stable"</span> | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.<span class="hljs-keyword">list</span>.d/docker.<span class="hljs-keyword">list</span> &gt; /dev/<span class="hljs-keyword">null</span> sudo apt-get update sudo apt-get install
docker-ce docker-ce-cli containerd.io</code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-1"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">PHP </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">php </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dan Anda memerlukan kode untuk menginstal GitLab runner. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Ada
 </font></font><a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/runner/install/" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">panduan penginstalan</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , dan tampilannya seperti ini…</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-javascript">curl -LJO <span class="hljs-string">"https://gitlab-runner-downloads.s3.amazonaws.com/latest/deb/gitlab-runner_amd64.deb"</span>
sudo dpkg -i gitlab-runner_amd64.deb rm
gitlab-runner_amd64.deb</code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-2"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">JavaScript </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">javascript </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<h2><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Registrasi</font></font></h2>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Setelah semuanya terinstal, Anda siap untuk mendaftarkan runner, dan menghubungkannya ke instance dan proyek GitLab.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Buka Pengaturan &gt;&gt; CI/CD pada proyek Anda. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Di bawah bagian "Pelari" Anda akan menemukan "token pendaftaran" yang harus Anda gunakan pada pelari.</font></font></p>
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large img-responsive"><img alt="" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/GitLab_runners_configuration_-_specific_runners.png" class=" img-responsive"></figure>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Token ini dapat digunakan dengan </font></font><code>gitlab-runner
register</code><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">perintah, bersama dengan nama yang diberikan pengguna dan beberapa opsi lain seperti </font></font><code>--limit</code><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">yang membatasi jumlah pekerjaan yang dapat dijalankan oleh pelari sekaligus.</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-javascript">sudo gitlab-runner
register -n \ --url https:<span class="hljs-comment">//gitlab.wikimedia.org/ \</span>
--registration-token xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx \ --executor docker \
--limit <span class="hljs-number">3</span> \ --name <span class="hljs-string">"gitlab-runner-addshore-1012-docker-01"</span> \
--docker-image <span class="hljs-string">"docker:19.03.15"</span> \
--docker-privileged \ --docker-volumes <span class="hljs-string">"/certs/client"</span></code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-3"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">JavaScript </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">javascript </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Anda sekarang akan melihat runner muncul di GitLab UI.</font></font></p>
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large img-responsive"><img alt="" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/GitLab_runners_configuration_-_specific_runners_1_success.png" class=" img-responsive"></figure>
<h2><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Konfigurasi Lebih Lanjut</font></font></h2>
<h3><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Kesesuaian</font></font></h3>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Meskipun kami menetapkan batas 3 pekerjaan untuk pelari saat mendaftarkannya. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Ini hanya konfigurasi pelari. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Sebuah node tunggal dan memiliki beberapa runner dari beberapa tipe (atau dari tipe yang sama). </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Jadi ada juga pengaturan konkurensi node/global yang perlu diubah.</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-javascript">sudo sed -i
<span class="hljs-string">'s/^concurrent =.*/concurrent =
3/'</span> <span class="hljs-string">"/etc/gitlab-runner/config.toml"</span> sudo
systemctl restart gitlab-runner</code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-4"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">JavaScript </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">javascript </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<h3><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Cermin buruh pelabuhan</font></font></h3>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Jika CI Anda akan menggunakan gambar dari Docker Hub atau registri lain yang memberlakukan batasan, atau jika Anda ingin mempercepat CI, Anda mungkin ingin menjalankan dan mendaftarkan mirror docker lokal.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Sekali lagi, Anda dapat </font></font><a href="https://about.gitlab.com/blog/2020/10/30/mitigating-the-impact-of-docker-hub-pull-requests-limits/" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">mengikuti posting blog untuk penyiapan di sini</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , atau melakukan sesuatu seperti ini…</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Buat cermin dalam wadah…</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-javascript">sudo docker run -d -p
<span class="hljs-number">6000</span>:<span class="hljs-number">5000</span> \ -e
REGISTRY_PROXY_REMOTEURL=https:<span class="hljs-comment">//registry-1.docker.io \</span> --restart always \
--name registry registry:<span class="hljs-number">2</span></code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-5"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">JavaScript </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">javascript </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dapatkan alamat IP dari host…</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs">hostname --ip-address</code></div>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Tambahkan mirror ke konfigurasi docker deamon…</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-xml">sudo echo
'{"registry-mirrors": ["http://<span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">CUSTOM</span> <span class="hljs-attr">IP</span>&gt;</span>:<span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">PORT</span>&gt;</span>"]}'
&gt; /etc/docker/daemon.json sudo service docker
restart</code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-6"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">HTML, XML </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">xml </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dan juga daftarkan di konfigurasi runner, yang harus Anda temukan di </font></font><code>/etc/gitlab-runner/config.toml</code><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font><a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ee/ci/docker/using_docker_build.html#enable-registry-mirror-for-dockerdind-service" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">lihat dokumen ini mengapa ini juga diperlukan</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> )</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-javascript">[[runners.docker.services]] name =
<span class="hljs-string">"docker:19.03.15-dind"</span> command =
[<span class="hljs-string">"--registry-mirror"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"http://&lt;CUSTOM
IP&gt;:&lt;PORT&gt;"</span>]</code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-7"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">JavaScript </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">javascript </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Akhirnya restart pelari untuk terakhir kalinya…</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs">sudo systemctl restart
gitlab-runner</code></div>
<h2><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Contoh CI</font></font></h2>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Anda kemudian dapat mengonfigurasi beberapa pekerjaan yang sangat mendasar menggunakan file konfigurasi GitLab CI untuk proyek tersebut.</font></font></p>
<pre class="wp-block-code"></pre>
<div><code class="hljs language-javascript">image:
docker:<span class="hljs-number">19.03</span><span class="hljs-number">.15</span> <span class="hljs-attr">variables</span>:
DOCKER_TLS_CERTDIR: <span class="hljs-string">"/certs"</span>
<span class="hljs-attr">services</span>: - name:
docker:<span class="hljs-number">19.03</span><span class="hljs-number">.15</span>-dind <span class="hljs-attr">docker_system_info</span>: only: - web <span class="hljs-attr">stage</span>: check <span class="hljs-attr">script</span>: - docker system info <span class="hljs-attr">docker_hub_quota_check</span>: only: - web <span class="hljs-attr">stage</span>: check <span class="hljs-attr">image</span>: alpine:latest <span class="hljs-attr">before_script</span>: - apk add curl jq <span class="hljs-attr">script</span>: - | TOKEN=$(curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://auth.docker.io/token?service=registry.docker.io&amp;scope=repository:ratelimitpreview/test:pull"</span>
| jq --raw-output .token) &amp;&amp; curl --head --header <span class="hljs-string">"Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN"</span> <span class="hljs-string">"https://registry-1.docker.io/v2/ratelimitpreview/test/manifests/latest"</span>
<span class="hljs-number">2</span>&gt;&amp;<span class="hljs-number">1</span></code></div>
<pre><small class="shcb-language" id="shcb-language-8"><span class="shcb-language__label"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Bahasa kode: </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__name"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">JavaScript </font></font></span> <span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__slug"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">javascript </font></font></span><span class="shcb-language__paren"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></span></small></pre>
<h2><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Gotcha &amp; Membaca</font></font></h2>
<ul>
<li><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Contoh GitLab Wikimedia saat ini masih </font></font><a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/GitLab/Roadmap" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">dalam proses</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> .</font></font></li>
<li><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Jika menggunakan gambar dari Docker Hub batasnya bisa mengganggu. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Selain cermin, ada juga dokumentasi untuk menyediakan kunci untuk Docker Hub atau registri lain. </font><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">( </font></font><a href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/T288377" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">T288377</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> )</font></font></li>
<li>Depending on your CI, 20GB of disk can fill up quite quickly.
While running at a concurrency of 4 I would occasionally hit disk
limitations.</li>
<li>When people open merge requests from forks <a href="https://docs.gitlab.com/ee/ci/pipelines/merge_request_pipelines.html#run-pipelines-in-the-parent-project-for-merge-requests-from-a-forked-project" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">CI will not and
can not run using the project runners</a>.</li>
<li>Default caching is done per project, per runner, per job /
concurrency slot. This can lead to a lot of duplication unless a
shared cache is used!</li>
</ul>
<p>The post <a href="https://addshore.com/2021/11/mwcli-ci-in-wikimedia-gitlab-docker-in-docker/" rel="nofollow">mwcli CI in Wikimedia GitLab (docker in docker)</a>
appeared first on <a href="https://addshore.com/" rel="nofollow">Addshore</a>.</p>
        </div>
    </div>
</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://blog.legoktm.com/2021/11/01/generating-rust-types-for-mediawiki-api-responses.html">Generating Rust types for MediaWiki API responses</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">06:50, Monday, 01 2021 November UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>I just released version 0.2.0 of the <a href="https://lib.rs/crates/mwapi_responses">mwapi_responses</a> crate.
It automatically generates Rust types based on the query parameters
specified for use in MediaWiki API requests. If you're not familiar
with the MediaWiki API, I suggest you play around with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:ApiSandbox">API sandbox</a>.
It is highly dynamic, with the user specifying query parameters and
values for each property they wanted returned.</p>
<p>For example, if you wanted a page's categories, you'd use
<code>action=query&amp;prop=categories&amp;titles=[...]</code>. If
you just wanted basic page metadata you'd use
<code>prop=info</code>. For information about revisions, like who
made specific edits, you'd use <code>prop=revisions</code>. And so
on, for all the different types of metadata. For each property
module, you can further filter what properties you want. If under
info, you wanted the URL to the page, you'd use
<code>inprop=url</code>. If you wanted to know the user who created
the revision, you'd use <code>rvprop=user</code>. For the most
part, each field in the response can be toggled on or off using
various prop parameters. These parameters can be combined, so you
can just get the exact data that your use-case needs, nothing
extra.</p>
<p>For duck-typed languages like Python, this is pretty convenient.
You know what fields you've requested, so that's all you access.
But in Rust, it means you either need to type out the entire
response struct for each API query you make, or just rely on the
dynamic nature of <code>serde_json::Value</code>, which means
you're losing out on the fantastic type system that Rust
offers.</p>
<p>But what I've been working on in <code>mwapi_responses</code> is
a third option: having a Rust macro generate the response structs
based on the specified query parameters. Here's an example from the
documentation:</p>
<div class="highlight">
<pre><code><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">mwapi_responses</span>::<span class="n">prelude</span>::<span class="o">*</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="cp">#[query(</span>
<span class="cp">    prop=</span><span class="s">"info|revisions"</span><span class="cp">,</span>
<span class="cp">    inprop=</span><span class="s">"url"</span><span class="cp">,</span>
<span class="cp">    rvprop=</span><span class="s">"ids"</span>
<span class="cp">)]</span>
<span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Response</span><span class="p">;</span>
</code></pre></div>
<p>This expands to roughly:</p>
<div class="highlight">
<pre><code><span class="cp">#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Deserialize)]</span>
<span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Response</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">batchcomplete</span>: <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(rename = </span><span class="s">"continue"</span><span class="cp">)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">continue_</span>: <span class="nc">HashMap</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">query</span>: <span class="nc">ResponseBody</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="p">}</span><font></font>
<font></font>
<span class="cp">#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Deserialize)]</span>
<span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">ResponseBody</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">pages</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">ResponseItem</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="p">}</span><font></font>
<font></font>
<span class="cp">#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Deserialize)]</span>
<span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">ResponseItem</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">canonicalurl</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">contentmodel</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">editurl</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">fullurl</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">lastrevid</span>: <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">length</span>: <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">missing</span>: <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">new</span>: <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">ns</span>: <span class="kt">i32</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">pageid</span>: <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">pagelanguage</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">pagelanguagedir</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">pagelanguagehtmlcode</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">redirect</span>: <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">title</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">touched</span>: <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">String</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">revisions</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">ResponseItemrevisions</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="p">}</span><font></font>
<font></font>
<span class="cp">#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Deserialize)]</span>
<span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">ResponseItemrevisions</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">parentid</span>: <span class="kt">u32</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">revid</span>: <span class="kt">u32</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</code></pre></div>
<p>It would be a huge pain to have to write that out by hand every
time, so having the macro do it is really convenient.</p>
<p>The crate is powered by <a href="https://gitlab.com/legoktm/mwapi/-/tree/master/mwapi_responses_derive/data">
JSON metadata files</a> for each API module, specifying the
response fields and which parameters need to be enabled to have
them show up in the output. And there are some uh, creative methods
on how to represent Rust types in JSON so they can be spit out by
the macro. So far I've been writing the JSON files by hand by
testing each parameter out manually and then reading the MediaWiki
API source code. I suspect it's possible to automatically generate
them, but I haven't gotten around to that yet.</p>
<h2>Using enums?</h2>
<p>So far the goal has been to faithfully represent the API output
and directly map it to Rust types. This was my original goal and I
think a worthwhile one because it makes it easy to figure out what
the macro is doing. It's not really convenient to dump the structs
the macro creates (you need a tool like <a href="https://lib.rs/crates/cargo-expand">cargo-expand</a>), but if you
can see the API output, you know that the macro is generating the
exact same thing, but using Rust types.</p>
<p>There's a big downside to this, which is mostly that we're not
able to take full advantage of the Rust type system. In the example
above, lastrevid, length, pageid and touched are all typed using
<code>Option&lt;T&gt;</code>, because if the page is missing, then
those fields will be absent. But that means we need to
<code>.unwrap()</code> on every page after checking the value of
the missing property. It would be much better if we had
ResponseItem split into two using an enum, one for missing pages
and the other for those that exist.</p>
<div class="highlight">
<pre><code><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">ResponseItem</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Missing</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">ResponseItemMissing</span><span class="p">),</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Exists</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">ResposneItemExists</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</code></pre></div>
<p>This would also be useful for properties like
<code>rvprop=user|userid</code>. Currently setting that property
results in something like:</p>
<div class="highlight">
<pre><code><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">ResponseItemrevisions</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">anon</span>: <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">user</span>: <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">String</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="cp">#[serde(default)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">userhidden</span>: <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">userid</span>: <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</code></pre></div>
<p>Again, <code>Option&lt;T&gt;</code> is being used for the case
where the user is hidden, and those properties aren't available.
Instead we could have something like:</p>
<div class="highlight">
<pre><code><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">RevisionUser</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Hidden</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Visible</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">username</span>: <span class="nb">String</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">id</span>: <span class="kt">u32</span> <span class="p">}</span><span class="w">   </span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</code></pre></div>
<p>(Note that anon can be figured out by looking at <code>id ==
0</code>.) Again, this is much more convenient than the faithful
representation of JSON.</p>
<p>I'm currently assuming these kinds of enums can be made to work
with serde, or maybe we'll need some layer on top of that. I'm also
still not sure whether we want to lose the faithful representation
aspect of this.</p>
<h2>Next steps</h2>
<p>The main next step is to get this crate used in some real world
projects and see how people end up using it and what the
awkward/bad parts are. One part I've found difficult so far is that
these types are literally just types, there's no integration with
any API library, so it's all up to the user on how to figure that
out. There's also currently no logic to help with continuing
queries, I might look into adding some kind of merge() function to
help with that in the future.</p>
<p>I have some very very <a href="https://gitlab.com/legoktm/mwapi/-/commit/579d0f133c53e5cf9ff9ea658a5eca8208fe38d1">
proof-of-concept integration</a> code with my mwbot project, more
on that to come in a future blog post.</p>
<p>Contributions are welcome in all forms! For
questions/discussion, feel free to join
<code>#wikimedia-rust:libera.chat</code> (via Matrix or IRC) or use
the project's issue tracker.</p>
<p>To finish on a more personal note, this is easily the most
complex Rust code I've written so far. proc-macros are super
powerful, but it's super easy to get lost writing code that just
writes more code. It feels like it's been through at least 3 or 4
rounds of complex refactoring, each taking advantage of new Rust
things I learn, generally making the code better and more robust.
The <a href="https://legoktm.gitlab.io/mwapi/coverage/">code
coverage metrics</a> are off because it's split between two crates,
the code is actually fully 100% covered by integration+unit
tests.</p>
        </div>
    </div>

Wikimedia technical community. Please tell other users about these
changes. Not all changes will affect you. <a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News/2021/44" title="m:Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News/2021/44">Translations</a> are
available.</p>
<p><b>Recent changes</b></p>
<ul>
<li>There is a limit on the amount of emails a user can send each
day. This limit is now global instead of per-wiki. This change is
to prevent abuse. <a class="external autonumber" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/T293866">[1]</a></li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li><img alt="Recurrent item" height="16" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Octicons-sync.svg/12px-Octicons-sync.svg.png" title="Recurrent item" width="12" class=" img-responsive"> The <a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/MediaWiki_1.38/wmf.7" title="mw:MediaWiki 1.38/wmf.7">new version</a> of MediaWiki will be on

non-Wikipedia wikis and some Wikipedias from 3 November. It will be
on all wikis from 4 November (<a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/MediaWiki_1.38/Roadmap" title="mw:MediaWiki 1.38/Roadmap">calendar</a>).</li>

        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://weeklyosm.eu/archives/14940">weeklyOSM 588</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">11:04, Sunday, 31 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>19/10/2021-25/10/2021</p>
<div class="wp-caption alignnone img-responsive" style="width: 970px;">
<p class="wp-caption-text"><img alt="lead picture" height="539" src="https://i0.wp.com/weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2021/10/588_T_DE.png?resize=719%2C539&amp;ssl=1" width="719" class=" img-responsive"></p>
<p class="wp-caption-text">OpenData and OpenStreetMap [<a href="https://weeklyosm.eu/feed#wn588_25769"><sup>1</sup></a>] ©
Pascal Neis © <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/copyright">OpenStreetMap
contributors</a></p>
</div>
<h2 id="wn588_mapping">Mapping</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25770">Pascal Neis <a href="https://twitter.com/pascal_n/status/1452305983955427347?t=l71sCt8euZkvkPksdC1IgA&amp;s=19">
tweeted</a> that his ‘Unmapped Places of OSM’ has been
updated. A total of 331,000 places have been identified this year,
compared with 339,000 by the same time last year.</li>
<li id="wn588_25754">Christian Rogel, who recently bought an
electrically assisted tricycle, <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-fr/2021-October/104621.html">
suggested</a> <img alt="(fr)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/fr.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-fr/2021-October/104621.html">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> that he will be able to help provide advice on tags which
would help tricyclists make use of existing cycle
infrastructure.</li>
<li id="wn588_25755">DENelson83 <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/DENelson83/diary/397876">started</a>
converting individually named bodies of water on the Atlantic coast
of Canada to relations. He set out his rationale, but has already
received some negative feedback.</li>
<li id="wn588_25775">Alec Schulze-Eckel <a href="http://k1z.blog.uni-heidelberg.de/2021/10/19/successful-end-of-the-25-mapathon-projec/">
reported</a> the successful end of the <a href="http://k1z.blog.uni-heidelberg.de/2020/07/06/kick-off-of-the-25-mapathon-project/">
25th mapathon project</a> that saw the the formation of a small but
solid group of German Red Cross (GRC) volunteers over the course of
the project.</li>
<li id="wn588_25793">MKnight <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/MKnight/diary/397921">shared</a>
<img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/MKnight/diary/397921">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> his experience of guardrail mapping.</li>
<li id="wn588_25772">CzerwonyPazdzierz <a href="https://forum.openstreetmap.org/viewtopic.php?id=74040">asked</a>
<img alt="(pl)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/pl.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://forum.openstreetmap.org/viewtopic.php?id=74040">
<img alt="de" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a>, in the forum, about the places that are best mapped on OSM.
Besides the individual suggestions in the thread about it, there
<a href="https://disaster.ninja/live/#id=67409d70-4810-41e1-89aa-e931a4d73599;position=0.7090701287638694,36.70929282889733;zoom=2.44836132655108;excluded=hotActivations-67409d70-4810-41e1-89aa-e931a4d73599,alert-shape-67409d70-4810-41e1-89aa-e931a4d73599,bivariate-custom_kontur_openstreetmap_building_quantity,bivariate-custom_kontur_openstreetmap_road_length,bivariate-custom_kontur_openstreetmap_antiquity,bivariate-custom_kontur_openstreetmap_mapping_activity,osm-users,mapbox_locator_overlay,OSM_Inspector-Addresses,opensnowmap-overlay,osm-gps;layer=osm-mapnik-black_and_white;overlays=bivariate-custom_kontur_openstreetmap_quantity">
is</a> also a map showing the ratio of OSM objects to population
density.</li>
<li id="wn588_25764">A request for comments has been made for
<a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/artwork_type%3Dmaypole">
<code>artwork_type=maypole</code></a>, an additional tag to
<code>man_made=maypole</code> for maypoles with artistic
merit.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_community">Community</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25752">China’s OpenStreetMap local community,
OSMChina, has <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-cn/2021-October/000151.html">
released</a> <img alt="(zhcn)" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/08/zh-cn-black.svg" class=" img-responsive">
 &gt; <a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-cn/2021-October/000151.html">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> their <a href="https://osmchina.org/">website</a> <img alt="(zhcn)" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/08/zh-cn-black.svg" class=" img-responsive">
 &gt; <a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://osmchina.org">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> and offer a <a href="https://map.osmchina.org/#map=4/36.3499/107.9297">tile service</a>
based on OSM-Carto style, but at the moment the site only contains
data for mainland China.</li>
<li id="wn588_25778">Mateusz Konieczny <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/hot/2021-October/015661.html">
asked</a> about the status of HOT Tasking Manager (TM) projects,
which triggered another discussion about mapping quality and the
coordination of TM organised editing projects. Arnalie Vicario from
HOT reacted by <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/hot/2021-October/015667.html">
sharing information</a> about the HOT Data Quality and Assurance
working groups and invited contributors to participate in the next
meeting on 4 November.</li>
<li id="wn588_25784">OSMF Board member Amanda McCann <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/%E1%9A%9B%E1%9A%90%E1%9A%8B%E1%9A%90%E1%9A%85%E1%9A%87%E1%9A%90%E1%9A%9C%20%F0%9F%8F%B3%EF%B8%8F%E2%80%8D%F0%9F%8C%88/diary/397884">
provided</a> her regular monthly activity update for
September.</li>
<li id="wn588_25781">BryDee <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/BryDee/diary/397881">reported</a>
that the HOT Open Mapping Hub – Asia Pacific (OMH-AP) have
signed a letter of intent with the Asia Pacific Region branch
(WSB/APR) of the secretariat about working together with the World
Organization of the Scout Movement (WOSM). The initial agreement is
for three years. BryDee sees a lot of interest from the Scouts and
more importantly 30 million potential OSM mappers.</li>
<li id="wn588_25787">GOwin <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/GOwin/diary/397904">reported</a>
that OSMaPaaralan tasks are complete and more than 39,129 schools
have been mapped and verified in 2 years and 22 days.</li>
<li id="wn588_25762">Someone on the #osm IRC channel noticed that
if anyone mentions ‘OpenStreetMap’ in a YouTube video
comment, the post is immediately blocked. Simon Poole tweeted about
it <a href="https://twitter.com/sp8962/status/1451139404597170178">here</a>.</li>
<li id="wn588_25790">Lejun <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/Lejun/diary/397913">is
looking</a> for an app to map building facades. He describes his
desired criteria and evaluates possible tools in terms of their
suitability for this purpose.</li>
<li id="wn588_25783">martien-vdg <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/martien-vdg/diary/397882">wrote</a>
about his ideas on how to improve the mapping quality of new
mappers.</li>
<li id="wn588_25782">PlayzinhoAgro <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/PlayzinhoAgro/diary/397900">suggested</a>
a re-imagining of the OSM user profile page.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_openstreetmap_foundation">OpenStreetMap
Foundation</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25768">Dorothea Kazazi <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/osmf-talk/2021-October/008172.html">
has announced</a> that nominations for the OSMF Board election have
closed. There are six candidates for four board seats :
<ul>
<li>Guillaume Rischard, USA</li>
<li>Michal Migurski, USA</li>
<li>Amanda McCann, Germany</li>
<li>Mikel Maron, USA</li>
<li>Roland Olbricht, Germany</li>
<li>Bryan Housel, USA.</li>
</ul>
<p>Members can continue <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Talk:Foundation/AGM21/Election_to_Board#Community_questions_to_OSMF_board_candidates.2C_upon_which_the_official_set_will_be_based">
adding their questions</a> and information about the candidates is
available on the <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Foundation/AGM21/Election_to_Board#Candidates">
Candidate 2021</a> wiki page.</p>
<p>Voting information and proposed resolutions are detailed on the
<a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Foundation/AGM21/Election_to_Board">
Annual General Meeting 2021</a> wiki page.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_events">Events</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25785">Never been to Perth, Australia? Just <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/Sam%20Wilson/diary/397894">join</a>
The FOSS4G SotM Oceania Perth Hub conference with an OSM workshop
all day on Saturday 13 November.</li>
<li id="wn588_25758">State of the Map Africa 2021 is <a href="https://2021.stateofthemap.africa/">happening</a> online 19 to 21
November. Registration is open and Geoffrey Kateregga <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-africa/2021-October/000705.html">
has invited</a> applications for internet data scholarships to
enable remote participation for those who need it. The application
form is <a href="https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLScddbcFYQiN8roTiH1m3H7sS6ESBa6EKjquAwTvn18VC-IDgA/viewform">
online</a>.</li>
<li id="wn588_25788">The LCCWG <a href="https://blog.openstreetmap.org/2021/10/24/youre-invited-to-the-2021-local-chapters-and-communities-congress/">
extended</a> an invitation to leaders and members of OpenStreetMap
local communities to attend the 2021 Local Chapters and Communities
Congress, which will be held virtually on Saturday 6 November.
Representatives of other OSM user groups are also welcome.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_osm_research">OSM research</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25759">John Bryant, of the Overseas Development
Institute, has <a href="https://odi.org/en/publications/digital-mapping-and-inclusion-in-humanitarian-response/">
released</a> a working paper <em>Digital mapping and inclusion in
humanitarian response</em>. He notes that maps can contribute to
‘distancing’ and remote management of responses. Some
humanitarians interviewed also observed that a map frequently
becomes the end product rather than the ‘beginning of a
conversation’.</li>
<li id="wn588_25774">Hao Li <a href="http://k1z.blog.uni-heidelberg.de/2021/10/20/automatic-mapping-of-national-surface-water-with-openstreetmap-and-sentinel-2-msi-data-using-deep-learning/">
introduced</a> a <a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0303243421002786">
paper</a> that proposes an automatic surface water mapping workflow
by training a deep residual neural network (ResNet) based on
OpenStreetMap data and Sentinel-2 multispectral data and using the
Simple Non-Iterative Clustering (SNIC) superpixel algorithm for
generating object-based training samples. As part of the paper, a
case study was conducted that provides comprehensive insights into
how to best explore the synergy of volunteered geographic
information (VGI) and machine learning (ML) of Earth observation
(EO) data in a large-scale surface water mapping task.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_maps">Maps</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25773">The <a href="https://heigit.org/big-spatial-data-analytics-en/ohsome/">HeiGIT
ohsome team</a> is <a href="http://k1z.blog.uni-heidelberg.de/2021/10/22/2021-volcanic-eruption-in-la-palma-spain-continues-explore-the-temporal-changes-of-the-lava-field-in-openstreetmap-on-ohsomehex/">
extracting</a> full history OSM data of the volcanic eruption on La
Palma (Spain) and its constantly growing lava field to help keep
OSM up to date. Temporally explore the data, including every single
map edit, <a href="https://ohsome.org/apps/osm-history-explorer/#/volcano_eruption_la_palma_spain_202109/2021-10-21T06:01:12Z%2F2021-10-21T14:00:00Z/13/28.616173745603703/-17.89821350736635">
here</a>.</li>
<li id="wn588_25765">Web developer and artist <a href="https://www.hanshack.com/">Hans Hack</a> has <a href="https://hanshack.com/strassenkrieg">created</a> <img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive"> a
map that displays the ‘War Traces in Berlin Street
Names’ on an OSM base map. The historical eras (Prussia,
Empire …) are colour-coded and it can be filtered by a wide
variety of viewpoints.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_open_data">Open Data</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25769">Pascal Neis <a href="https://twitter.com/pascal_n/status/1450023559603146753?s=20">showed</a>
how helpful ‘live’ information can be displayed with
the help of free data and free software. For his implementation
‘<a href="https://opendata.gi.hs-mainz.de/parkingmainz/#13/50.0032/8.2693">utilization
of parking garages and traffic situation in Mainz</a>‘
<img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive">, he also
uses the OSM base map.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_software">Software</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25789">Bryan Housel <a href="https://twitter.com/bhousel/status/1452806915151605762/photo/1">announced</a>
the release of RapiD <a href="https://github.com/facebookincubator/RapiD/blob/main/CHANGELOG.md#118">
1.1.8</a>, which includes performance improvements and
bugfixes.</li>
<li id="wn588_25771"><a href="https://github.com/onthegomap/flatmap">Flatmap</a> is a tool that
generates Mapbox Vector Tiles from geographic data sources like
OpenStreetMap. Vector tiles contain raw point, line, and polygon
geometries that clients such as MapLibre can use to render custom
maps (<a href="https://onthegomap.github.io/flatmap-demo/">demo</a>).</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_programming">Programming</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25766">The Overpass API <a href="https://dev.overpass-api.de/blog/way_based_areas.html">treats</a>
closed ways not only as ways but also as areas now.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_did_you_know_…">Did you know …</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25776">… the key <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Key%3Awinter_service"><code>winter_service=*</code></a>
is available? The key can be used to map paths or areas that do not
have winter service, as well as those which are regularly cleared
of snow and ice.</li>
<li id="wn588_25792">… the <a href="https://www.nunav.net/">NUNAV Navigation</a> app for cars? It
combines OpenStreetMap with real-time traffic data in Germany,
Austria and Switzerland (<strong>for now</strong>) and is available
in the app stores in a number of European countries. Your route is
continuously recalculated based on traffic during a trip. The app
has no ads or trackers and the <a href="https://www.nunav.net/data-privacy">GPS location data</a>
<img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive"> is only
used for traffic aggregation. You can give the routing a try on the
website of the <a href="https://www.vmz-niedersachsen.de/navigation">traffic control
centre Lower Saxony</a> <img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive">.</li>
<li id="wn588_25791">… there is a list of <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Software">software</a> for OSM
users at home or on the road?</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn588_other_“geo”_things">Other
“geo” things</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn588_25760">Satellite imagery firm Planet Labs is ten
years old, and expecting to go public shortly with a valuation of
around $2.8 billion. Ari Lewis <a href="https://twitter.com/amlewis4/status/1450648248666886147">gave</a>
a potted history of the company in a Twitter thread.</li>
<li id="wn588_25746">Carlo Ratti <a href="https://theconversation.com/cellphone-data-shows-that-people-navigate-by-keeping-their-destinations-in-front-of-them-even-when-thats-not-the-most-efficient-route-170004">
found</a> that people (without navigation software) tend to follow
their intuition rather than the most effective path when choosing
routes, after analysing mobile phone data at <a href="https://www.mit.edu/">MIT</a>.</li>
<li id="wn588_25756">Shaun McDonald <a href="https://blog.shaunmcdonald.me.uk/2021/10/cycle-friendliness-of-bramford-lane-roadworks/">
examined</a> the cycle-friendliness of roadworks during the
installation of a new gas main.</li>
<li id="wn588_25777">TomTom <a href="https://www.tomtom.com/blog/maps/the-battle-for-quality-maps/">described</a>
how they have made progress in improving quality with their
MapMetrics system by removing bad data, e.g. filtering out GPS
tracks from people on trains. The map data used during the process
is based on OpenStreetMap.</li>
</ul>

</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://commonists.wordpress.com/2021/10/29/where-is-the-technical-volunteer-support-in-the-wikiverse/">Where is the technical volunteer support in the Wikiverse?</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">21:40, Friday, 29 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>Volunteer support is a major theme in the Wikimedia movement,
and <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Volunteer_Supporters_Network">a
typical endeavour of many affiliates</a>. Content contributors are
supported in many ways&nbsp;− Wikipedia writers get access to
reference books, Wikimedia Commons photographers to <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Commons:Wikimedia_Sverige#Supporting_volunteers">
equipment and accreditations</a>, contest organizers to project
management support, etc.</p>
<p>Yet, to me there seems to be a major blindspot when it comes to
technical contributors.</p>
<p>By technical contributors, I encompass all people contributing
to server-side scripting (templates and modules), client-side
scripting (user-scripts and gadgets), autonomous editing programs
(bots), desktop and web applications, etc.</p>
<h2>Existing support</h2>
<p>Here I will try to draw a (likely non-exhaustive) map of the
existing support.</p>
<h3><strong>Technical infrastructure</strong></h3>
<p>The Wikimedia Foundation (WMF) provides technical
infrastructure:</p>
<ul>
<li>to run the tools, eg web-apps and bots via <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Main_Page">Cloud VPS and
Toolforge</a></li>
<li>to support the development life-cycle: issue tracking,
code-hosting, code-review, build &amp; testing, deployment − with
Gerrit, Phabricator and Jenkins.</li>
</ul>
<p>While these platforms have their shortcomings (indeed, many
volunteer developers avoid them altogether), I believe they are an
amazing proposition. I also believe they are well supported: hang
out on IRC asking for help for your Toolforge tool, and you will
most certainly get it, whether from WMF staff, volunteers, or WMF
staff with their volunteer hat.</p>
<h3><strong>Events</strong></h3>
<p>The WMF, generally in partnership with an affiliate, has long
been organizing <a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Hackathons">hackathons</a> −
the Wikimedia hackathon around May, and the Wikimania one around
July/August (other such events exist, such as the Dutch
TechStorm).</p>
<p>I think hackathons are amazing&nbsp;− as I <a href="https://commonists.wordpress.com/2019/07/06/the-story-of-integraality-or-my-quest-to-make-it-at-the-wikimedia-hackathon/">
wrote before</a>, they are great at creating an atmosphere suited
to get work done.</p>
<h3><strong>Motivation &amp; appreciation</strong></h3>
<p>A <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Volunteer_Supporters_Network/Resources#Our_own_resources">
key tenet of the volunteer support</a>, this has seen some welcome
progress with the notable creation of the <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Coolest_Tool_Award">Coolest Tool
Award</a>.</p>
<h3><strong>Money</strong></h3>
<p>Ah, this is often where it ends: a question “What about
VeryImportantTool” is likely to elicit an answer along the
lines of “This tool is volunteer-developed, and not supported
by BigOrganization. We would be happy to consider a grant request
to work on it though!”</p>
<p>While grants are useful, and have certainly helped the creation
and enhancement of great tools (both in the Wikiverse and in other
open movements like OpenStreetMap¹), I think this answer is
reductive and inappropriate in many cases. The main reason I see is
that most often, <strong>when time or motivation are lacking, money
will not buy either</strong>. Some tool developers may be
self-employed freelancers, or be between jobs, with the flexibility
to set aside a few weeks/months supported by a grant ; not so much
if one is regularly employed. Timing can also be tricky: some
grants have cycles, which may not fit the (work-)life of
people.</p>
<h2>So what is missing?</h2>
<p>I believe that what is missing in tool development is more
collaboration. <strong>It takes a village to raise a tool</strong>
− and various specialties ranging from product ownership,
design, development, operations, testing, QA, security,
documentation… −&nbsp; yet more often than not, a
single person is behind a tool.</p>
<h3>Staff support</h3>
<p>It has been suggested before that WMF should take over part of
the duties related to a tool − typically the operations (of
tools like PetScan) but <a href="https://lists.wikimedia.org/hyperkitty/list/design@lists.wikimedia.org/thread/NMNXC62R4E3ER23JLNYK775OMUZY65R5/#DDMFTNOY5U6W3C4PLBD3GVFYZWQBPK53">
UX/design had also been suggested</a>.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Historically, I think it fair to say WMF has not been keen on
doing so. I can see good reasons to avoid that (different
priorities, limited resources, not so easy to adopt foreign and
potentially messy codebases, perhaps fear of cannibalizing
volunteer efforts), but also bad ones (wrong sense of priorities,
<a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Talk:Community_Tech/Event_Metrics#On_developing_new_outreach_tools">
NIH syndrome</a>).</p>
<p>I can see how staff taking over operations of a major tool, or
having a <a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/User_experience_review_queue">UX
review queue</a>, might not be sustainable. But I am convinced that
<strong>there is space for a technical counterpart to the Volunteer
Support for content contributors.</strong></p>
<p>This crystalized to me when (story time) following the <a href="https://github.com/pypa/pipenv/issues/3369">pipenv 2018
release</a> − where <a href="https://www.harihareswara.net/sumana/">Sumana Harihareswara</a>
(who once upon a time worked at WMF, interestingly enough) stepped
in to help the maintainers put together a well-overdue release of a
major piece of the Python ecosystem. Sumana called it
“<a href="https://www.harihareswara.net/sumana/2021/06/07/0#coaching-and-cheerleading">Coaching
and cheerleading</a>”:</p>
<blockquote class="wp-block-quote">
<p>An external perspective can help a lot. You can be that person.
Whether you call yourself a sidekick, a project manager, a
cheerleader, a coach, or something else, you can be a supportive
accountability partner who helps with the bits that maintainers are
not great at, or don’t have time for. And you don’t
have to know the project codebase to do this, or be a feature-level
developer – the only pipenv code I touched was the docs.</p>
<cite>Sumana Harihareswara</cite></blockquote>
<p>We could really use some professional coaches and
cheerleaders.</p>
<p>(Speaking only for myself, as the developer of the moderately
successful integraality (and ex-co-maintainer of the the <a href="http://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Commons:monuments%20database">monuments
database</a>) − no smash hits, but somewhat relied upon tools
− I can see how having someone checking in on me once every
couple of months, to help me plan/organize work, could be very
valuable).</p>
<h3>Being the village</h3>
<p>As I outlined above, there are many parts to tool development,
many of which are non-technical: handling bug reports, writing
documentation, prioritizing feature requests… We are an
amazing collaborative community − why isn’t there more
collaboration around tools? For example, when <a href="https://commonists.wordpress.com/2019/07/06/the-story-of-integraality-or-my-quest-to-make-it-at-the-wikimedia-hackathon/">
building integraality</a>, I experienced first-hand how delegating
product decisions helped:</p>
<blockquote class="wp-block-quote">
<p>Making the decisions on where to take the product and what red
lines to draw scope-wise is sometimes the hardest. This saved me
heaps of time, in the couple of instances where I was unsure how to
proceed. I wonder if this should be part of the hackathon setup
− every hacker being the “owner” or
“client” of the another’s project.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>This − again − crystalized with a recent story:
reading Magnus Manske’s <a href="http://magnusmanske.de/wordpress/?p=658">“The
Buggregator”</a> blog post. I could not help but feel deeply
sad: Magnus, a prolific developer of highly-popular tools, is so
overwhelmed with bug reports and feature requests, raised in many
different places, that he feels the need to write a tool to help
manage all of these. I could not help but think − why on
earth does he have to manage this communication influx all by
himself? Since his tools are so popular, surely there should be
many folks happy to help with this tool, or that one? When someone
reports a bug to Magnus on some random talk page or Telegram
channel, why isn’t there a volunteer happy to take over, ask
the necessary clarifications, file it in the canonical bug tracking
place (whichever that might be), prioritize it for later?</p>
<p>Of course, most of us will never churn in so many tools that we
need to write a bug aggregation platform ; but I think that
Magnus’ problems are everyone’s problems − just
magnified (magnufied?) ten times over.</p>
<p>In short, there should be more of a community active around a
popular tool − people helping out in particular with the
non-technical aspects.&nbsp;</p>
<p>I used to think that the lack of such community was somehow the
responsibility of the developer themself − that if you were
the single-maintainer on your Toolforge tool account, then you
should try a bit harder.</p>
<p>I have come around on this: we set out to develop software,
often to scratch our own itch, and not necessarily expecting
success ; we don’t sign up to do community building and
management on top. But that community does not seem to happen on
its own either: it seems that in this movement, <strong>we are more
prone to ask&nbsp;tool developers for help, than to ask whether
they need help.</strong></p>
<p>If so, then I think <em>this</em> should be the first and
foremost job of the professional technical volunteer support:
<strong>helping build up an active support network around a
tool</strong>. This may include recruiting co-developers, but I see
a real opportunity in engaging volunteers in non-technical
capacities, and <strong>structuring that engagement</strong> with
models and best practices. Far from cannibalizing volunteer
resources, this would rather fit nicely in our goal of <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Strategy/Wikimedia_movement/2018-20/Recommendations/Glossary#Capacity_building">
capacity building</a> and <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Strategy/Wikimedia_movement/2018-20/Recommendations/Increase_the_Sustainability_of_Our_Movement">
increasing the sustainability of our movement</a>.</p>
<h1>Conclusion</h1>
<p>In this post, I tried to map out the existing support for
technical contributors, and have made the case for professional
volunteer support, mirroring the practices and successes of support
for content contributors. Beyond a direct “coaching and
cheerleading”, this would entail recruiting and structuring
volunteer-based support networks around each tool.</p>
<p>This may find an echo at the existing big software-houses that
are WMF and WMDE, who may decide to create dedicated technical
volunteer support roles or teams − I would certainly welcome
it. But there are so many tools − I don’t think this is
a problem that can be solved centrally. After all, no one expects
WMF to help out individual content contributors in a particular
country or focus area − this is what affiliates have excelled
in.</p>
<p>Rather, the idea would rather play well with the <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Hubs">Hubs model</a> of support
structures that has been developed as part of the 2030 strategy: a
hypothetical “GLAM” thematic hub helping out on
GLAM-related tools, or a “Wikisource” hub on Wikisource
tools, etc.</p>
<p>Until then, in the spirit of decentralization and subsidiarity,
I rather hope that the idea might be taken up by all affiliates:
expanding their existing volunteer support to technical
contributors − one tool at a time.</p>
<hr class="wp-block-separator">
<p><em>This piece was in the works for a while ; the impetus to
finish out was ahead of the</em> <a href="https://pretalx.com/wdcon21/talk/9VZJVK/"><em>“Please
don’t get hit by a bus! Towards a resilient and sustainable
Wikidata tool ecosystem”</em></a> <em>session at WikidataCon
2021.</em></p>
<hr class="wp-block-separator">
<h2>Notes</h2>
<p><small>¹ <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Commons:Pattypan">Pattypan</a>
(<a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Grants:IEG/Batch_uploader_for_small_GLAM_projects">grant</a>)
immediately comes to my mind ; I also think of the <a href="https://github.com/streetcomplete/StreetComplete#sponsors">StreetComplete
project</a> (which I am quite fond of)</small></p>
        </div>

                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://thottingal.in/blog/2021/10/29/manjari-as-new-lipi-font/">Using Manjari as new orthography Malayalam font</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">14:30, Friday, 29 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>Manjari is a traditional orthography font for Malayalam. It has
large set of ligatures, vowel signs like /u/ get attached to its
corresponding consonants to form ligatures. But, sometimes there
are requirements to illustrate new orthography Malayalam content in
Manjari. Recently, Manjari was used to typeset an academic book
related to Malayalam script and it was required to show some
content in new orthography with detached vowel signs and detached
reph signs.</p>
        </div>
