        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://weeklyosm.eu/archives/14930">weeklyOSM 587</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">10:11, Sunday, 24 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>12/10/2021-18/10/2021</p>
<div class="wp-caption alignnone img-responsive" style="width: 1290px;">
<p class="wp-caption-text"><img alt="lead picture" height="719" src="https://i2.wp.com/weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2021/10/588_T_all.png?resize=719%2C719&amp;ssl=1" width="719" class=" img-responsive"></p>
<p class="wp-caption-text">OpenStreetMap France celebrated its 10th
birthday [<a href="https://weeklyosm.eu/feed#wn587_25730"><sup>1</sup></a>] ©
<a href="https://www.openstreetmap.fr/">OpenStreetMap
France</a></p>
</div>
<h2 id="wn587_mapping_campaigns">Mapping campaigns</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25761">The Planning Department of the Ministry of
Education in Madagascar, in collaboration with the UNESCO
International Institute for Educational Planning (IIEP-UNESCO) and
UN Mappers, is seeking to map the <a href="https://tasks.hotosm.org/explore?campaign=IIEP%20UNESCO">full road
network</a> of the Vakinankaratra region to make sure that the
journey to school for children can be as straightforward as
possible. The road network produced will then be processed using
the <a href="https://github.com/iiepdev/school-catchment-plugin">IIEP-UNESCO
school catchment plugin</a> to assess travel times. A <a href="https://www.eventbrite.it/e/mapathon-united-nations-for-madagascar-registration-193356884647">
mapathon</a> open to everyone will be held next Wednesday 27
October.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_mapping">Mapping</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25739">Mapillary’s change from API version 3 to
4 has apparently resulted in changed photo IDs, which had been
tagged in OSM on some objects with <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Key:mapillary"><code>mapillary=*</code></a>.
There is a discussion on the tagging mailing list about how to
handle the tag in the future. Mateusz Konieczny <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/tagging/2021-October/062637.html">
proposes</a> abolishing the tag if a changeover is not
possible.</li>
<li id="wn587_25740">Sebastian <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-de/2021-October/117483.html">
asked</a> <img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-de/2021-October/117483.html">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> the talk-de mailing list how to correctly record hydrants with
<a href="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/61/Hydrantenschild_rot_und_blau.jpg">
blue bordered signs</a> and if there is an already established
procedure.</li>
<li id="wn587_25747">DUGA humorously <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/DUGA/diary/397848">describes</a>
mapping practices that they believe are incorrect and offers better
solutions, which are also welcomed to be discussed in the
comments.</li>
<li id="wn587_25734">Requests have been made for comments on the
following proposals:
<ul>
<li><a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/Inlets_proposal">
<code>inlet=*</code></a> for tagging the details of where the flow
enters a culvert or pipeline.</li>
<li><a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/Avalanche-transceiver">
Avalanche transceiver training zones</a> for mapping areas where
skiers can practice using their avalanche beacon.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="wn587_25713">Voting has ended for the following proposals:
<ul>
<li><a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/fumarole"><code>
natural=fumarole</code></a>, to map an opening in our
planet’s crust, which emits steam and gases, was approved
with 16 votes for, 0 votes against and 0 abstentions.</li>
<li><a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/Multiple_landuse">
<code>landuse:secondary=*</code></a>, for mapping multiple land
uses in a single area, was not successful with 14 votes for, 23
votes against and 3 abstentions.</li>
<li><a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/Key:headlight">
<code>headlight=*</code></a>, for reflecting the legal requirement
on some roads to use your headlights, was approved with 28 votes
for, 1 vote against and 0 abstentions.</li>
<li><a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/key:foraging">
<code>foraging=*</code></a>, to indicate whether or not foraging
for plants/fruit/fungi etc. is permissible for a given location or
plant, was approved with 11 votes for, 0 votes against and 3
abstentions.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="wn587_25751">tffmh has <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/tffmh/diary/397874">reviewed</a>
the streets of <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/#map=14/51.4229/6.9049">Mühlheim
an der Ruhr</a> to make sure the <code>de:strassenschluessel</code>
(a street’s unique identifier) and etymology are
correct.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_community">Community</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25726">arnalielsewhere <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/arnalielsewhere/diary/397844">shared</a>
the collaboration project: ‘Localization as an Inclusion and
Participatory Enabler’, which aims to bridge the gap between
language and accessibility of HOT Humanitarian Open Mapping
resources. The project is in collaboration with local communities
and contributors from Vietnam, Madagascar, and Mozambique, as well
as the Open Mapping Hubs in the Asia-Pacific and East and Southern
Africa.</li>
<li id="wn587_25717">The HOT Open Mapping – Asia Pacific Hub
is launching <a href="https://www.hotosm.org/updates/launching-she-leads-and-she-inspires-women-in-leadership-program/">
‘She Leads and She Inspires’</a>, a programme that will
engage 100 women between December 2021 and June 2022.</li>
<li id="wn587_25743">Volunteers <a href="https://blog.openstreetmap.org/2021/10/17/looking-for-moderators-for-osm-lists/">
are needed</a> from all corners of the global OpenStreetMap
community to participate in the OSMF Moderation Team to lead
efforts to keep the lists safe, welcoming, and inclusive.</li>
<li id="wn587_25736">Many user accounts <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Talk:Proposed_features/Cryptocurrencies_with_payment_tag#Many_new_users_voting_in_this_proposal">
were created</a> in order to vote in the <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/Cryptocurrencies_with_payment_tag">
proposal</a> to include cryptocurrencies into the payment tag,
resulting in questioning whether it could be an issue or not and
how the voting system could be reduced to absurdity through mass
new user account creation.</li>
<li id="wn587_25748">Valerio Bozzolan <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/Valerio_Bozzolan/diary/397863">illustrated</a>
how he maps and locates veterinarians for rabbits <img alt="🐇" class="wp-smiley img-responsive" src="https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.1.0/72x72/1f407.png" style="height: 1em;"> with an expansion of a proposal submitted in 2012
to detail veterinary tagging.</li>
<li id="wn587_25728">Feye Andal <a href="https://feyeandal.me/blog/ym_regional_ambassador">reviewed</a> her
work as the Southeast Asia YouthMappers Ambassador in 2021. The
number of chapters in the region grew from four to nine.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_openstreetmap_foundation">OpenStreetMap
Foundation</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25753">Allan Mustard, current chair of the
OpenStreetMap Foundation board, <a href="https://twitter.com/allan_mustard/status/1450253068294045702">announced</a>
that he will not be standing for re-election.</li>
<li id="wn587_25723">On the OSMF-Talk mailing list, Dorothea Kazazi
<a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/osmf-talk/2021-October/008156.html">
announced</a> that questions to candidates in the next OSMF board
elections can be <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Talk:Foundation/AGM21/Election_to_Board">
submitted</a> on a OSM wiki page until 2 November.</li>
<li id="wn587_25724">The Openstreetmap Foundation Local Chapters
and Communities Working Group (LCCWG) is <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Foundation/Local_Chapters/Local_Chapters_Congress/2021">
inviting</a> you to the Local Chapters and Communities Congress
2021 on 6 November.</li>
<li id="wn587_25750">The Microgrants Committee has <a href="https://blog.openstreetmap.org/2021/10/17/report-by-the-osmf-microgrants-committee-on-the-trial-run-of-microgrants/">
submitted</a> a report on the trial run of the OSMF microgrants
programme. Project reports by grantees are also linked off the same
page.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_local_chapter_news">Local chapter news</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25730">[1] The France OSM community <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.fr/openstreetmap-france-fete-ses-10-ans/">
celebrated</a> <img alt="(fr)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/fr.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://www.openstreetmap.fr/openstreetmap-france-fete-ses-10-ans/">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> the 10<sup>th</sup> anniversary of the foundation of OSM-FR
with meetings linked by BigBlueButton. A special delegation
<a href="https://twitter.com/OSM_FR/status/1447612101187493888">visited</a>
the site of the meeting which created OSM France, and left a
(temporary) plaque.</li>
<li id="wn587_25731">The <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.us/2021/10/call-for-proposals-sotmus2022/">
call for proposals</a> of State of the Map US 2022 (1 to 3 April
2022 in Tucson, Arizona) is open until 17 December 2021.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_osm_research">OSM research</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25722">Siddharth Joshi et al. have published an
<a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/s41467-021-25720-2?error=cookies_not_supported&amp;code=b7603c99-58d5-47c0-94be-8b81b4774c3c">
article</a> in <em>Nature Communications</em> on a global
assessment of rooftop solar photovoltaic’s potential for
renewable electricity generation. The study used road and building
data from OpenStreetMap.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_humanitarian_osm">Humanitarian OSM</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25715">The HOT Disaster Services Team have <a href="https://www.hotosm.org/disaster-services/mediterranean-wildfires-2021-conclusion/">
shared</a> an after action report on the activation in response to
the Mediterranean Wildfires, sharing their internal assessment of
how the activation was carried out.</li>
<li id="wn587_25725">The HOT Quality Control and Assurance Working
Group has <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Humanitarian_OSM_Team/Working_groups/Data_Quality_Control_and_Assurance/Tasking_Manager_Project_Gardening">
started</a> a Tasking Manager Project Gardening Process wiki page
with the objective of defining the workflow for the administration
of the Tasking Manager, specifically the oversight of projects.
Phase 1 looks at archiving projects that no longer have a reason to
remain active on the Tasking Manager.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_maps">Maps</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25738"><a href="https://webkid.io/about">webkid</a>
have produced an OSM based map which shows the age of every
building in Berlin using a public dataset. The map <a href="https://interaktiv.morgenpost.de/so-alt-wohnt-berlin/">is used</a>
under the title – ‘Old or new building? So lives
Berlin’ – on an interactive site of the <em>Berliner
Morgenpost</em>.</li>
<li id="wn587_25718">Aishworya Shrestha from Kathmandu Living Labs
<a href="https://www.hotosm.org/updates/before-after-maps-visualizing-osm-mapping-contribution-over-time/">
announced</a> the launch of the <a href="https://beforeafter.baato.io/">Before-After Map</a> Query tool and
invited users to make maps of their own areas. This query tool
shows data for a place at two different points in time. Its main
objective is to compare how a particular area looks in two
different years, side by side, and show local mapping efforts over
a specific time period. Users must provide name and email details
to be notified once the map is generated.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_software">Software</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25721">The Geo Data Merger is a desktop open source
tool for <a href="https://funkeinteraktiv.github.io/geo-data-merger/">merging</a>
data from csv, json, geo- and topojson files.</li>
<li id="wn587_25678">During this year’s State of the Map,
Davey Lovin (user <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/mDav">mDav</a>) <a href="https://youtu.be/j6962TNkLTc?t=77">introduced</a> a webmap and
quality assurance tool for long distance hiking trails. <a href="https://superroute.org/">Superroute</a> aims to gather together a
community of hikers to maintain and improve the data quality of
these trails.</li>
<li id="wn587_25727">The <a href="https://a-b-street.github.io/docs/software/ungap_the_map/index.html">
A/B Street</a> traffic simulator now lets you reimagine your city
as it would be if designed for safe travel by bicycle. This
extension of the project aims to show how such changes to the road
network would impact travels citywide.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_programming">Programming</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25737">HeiGIT and HOT have partnered together and
extended the <a href="https://www.hotosm.org/updates/hot-merl-is-monitoring-osm-and-tasking-manager-projects/">
Humanitarian OSM Stats website</a> to help relay mapping statistics
to the public. It includes data, not only from HOT Tasking Manager
projects, but also from all the other OSM contributors.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_did_you_know_…">Did you know …</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25749">… that it <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/bryceco/diary/397864">is</a>
possible to run Go Map!! on your Mac?</li>
<li id="wn587_25641">… <a href="https://github.com/organicmaps/organicmaps#readme">Organic
Maps</a>? Another offline map app using OpenStreetMap data, forked
from MAPS.ME, it features no ads, no tracking, nor data
collection.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn587_other_“geo”_things">Other
“geo” things</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn587_25714">Google unnecessarily <a href="https://twitter.com/michael_fradley/status/1447842069255528448">continues
to censor</a> part of Israel after receiving updated imagery from
Airbus.</li>
</ul>

</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://addshore.com/2021/10/addwiki-php-libraries-3-0-0/?utm_source=rss&amp;utm_medium=rss&amp;utm_campaign=addwiki-php-libraries-3-0-0">addwiki php libraries 3.0.0</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">20:45, Saturday, 23 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>Back in 2014 I wrote a small collection of PHP libraries,
<a href="https://addshore.com/2015/12/mediawiki-api-base-2-0-0/">releasing
2.0.0 of the base library in 2015</a> for interacting with
MediaWiki and Wikibase. My goal back then was to create a stable
base that PHP bot frameworks could be built on, while also
experimenting with some framework like features in surrounding
libraries.</p>
<p>And now, version 3.0.0 has been released, with a couple of new
features, such as OAuth authentication, and lots of refactoring to
make the libraries easier to work with and contribute to.</p>
<div class="wp-block-jetpack-gif">
<figure class=" img-responsive">
<div class="wp-block-jetpack-gif-wrapper" style="padding-top: 65%;"></div>
</figure>
</div>
<span id="more-7875"></span>
<h2>Library usage</h2>
<p>I find it pretty hard to figure out how many people actually use
these libraries and if it is worth keeping them updated, but there
are a few notable projects that make use of them, particularly
<code>mediawiki-api-base</code> which is a simple client wrapping
Guzzle.</p>
<p>Packagist and Github metrics seem to hint that there is some
usage. Though I suspect that the download numbers mainly come from
usage in other projects CI setups.</p>
<figure class="wp-block-table img-responsive">
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Package</strong></td>
<td><strong>Github Stars</strong> <img alt="⭐" class="wp-smiley img-responsive" src="https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.1.0/72x72/2b50.png" style="height: 1em;"></td>
<td><strong>Packagist downloads in last 30 days</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="https://packagist.org/packages/addwiki/mediawiki-api-base" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">mediawiki-api-base</a></td>
<td>33</td>
<td><a href="https://packagist.org/packages/addwiki/mediawiki-api-base/stats" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">1248</a> (41 a
day)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="https://packagist.org/packages/addwiki/mediawiki-api" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">mediawiki-api</a></td>
<td>36</td>
<td><a href="https://packagist.org/packages/addwiki/mediawiki-api/stats" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">745</a> (24 a
day)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="https://packagist.org/packages/addwiki/wikibase-api" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">wikibase-api</a></td>
<td>20</td>
<td><a href="https://packagist.org/packages/addwiki/wikibase-api/stats" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">103</a> (3 a
day)</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</figure>
<p>And I can easily hunt out some notable usages (even if some are
mine):</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://github.com/wikisource/ws-search" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">wikisource/ws-search</a> – A simple search tool for
all Wikisources.</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/wikimedia/CopyPatrol" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">wikimedia/CopyPatrol</a> – The web interface for
Plagiabot (authored by @eranroz)</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/wikimedia/popularpages" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">wikimedia/popularpages</a> – Tool for generating
popular page reports for WikiProjects</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/samwilson/basildon" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">samwilson/basildon</a> – A static site
generator.</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/magnusmanske/quickstatements" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">magnusmanske/quickstatements</a> – The official repo
for the QuickStatements PHP/HTML/JS interface</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/UTRS2/utrs" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">UTRS2/utrs</a>
– Unblock Ticket Request System (v2) used on Wikimedia
projects</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/Archi-Strasbourg/mediawiki-mail-recentchanges" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Archi-Strasbourg/mediawiki-mail-recentchanges</a> –
Send recent changes to every user of your wiki</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/addshore/twitter-wikidatameter" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">addshore/twitter-wikidatameter</a> – A Twitter bot
powered by Github Actions tweeting Wikidata milestones</li>
</ul>
<p>So bring on a little refresh, in the form of version 3.0!</p>
<h2>What’s changed for users?</h2>
<p>The libraries now require PHP 7.4+ and have had typing added
throughout.</p>
<p>All libraries have updated namespaces to follow <a href="https://www.php-fig.org/psr/psr-4/" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">PSR4</a>. The base
library uses the namespace <code>Addwiki\Mediawiki\Api</code> and
which is shared by <code>mediawiki-api</code> which builds on top
of it. The <code>wikibase-api</code> library takes the names space
<code>Addwiki\Wikibase</code> etc.</p>
<p>The base library saw some additions such as a
<code>RestApi</code> and OAuth authentication has been added to all
APIs.</p>
<p>The simple username and password based auth has been replaced by
an <code>AuthMethod</code> interface. This interface has a few
implementations including <code>UserAndPassword</code>,
<code>UserAndPasswordWithDomain</code>, <code>NoAuth</code> and
<code>OAuthOwnerConsumer</code>. These can be used when creating an
API service object to decide how to authenticate with it.</p>
<h2>What’s changed for addwiki devs?</h2>
<p>If you want to contribute to these libraries, you’ll now
find that all development happens as part of a monorepo in <a href="https://github.com/addwiki/addwiki" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">addwiki/addwiki</a>.</p>
<p>This should make contribution easier, as no complex inter
library dependencies need to be thought of. This should also lead
to making more releases as things are iteratively added or
improved, as the release process is much simpiler.</p>
<p>For an overview of the workflows, make sure you read the
<a href="https://github.com/addwiki/addwiki" rel="external noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">README</a>!</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://addshore.com/2021/10/addwiki-php-libraries-3-0-0/" rel="nofollow">addwiki php libraries 3.0.0</a> appeared first on
<a href="https://addshore.com/" rel="nofollow">Addshore</a>.</p>
        </div>
    </div>
</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://wikiedu.org/blog/2021/10/22/wikipedia-as-science-communication/">Wikipedia as science communication</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">15:38, Friday, 22 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p><em>Yug Chandra Saraswat is currently enrolled in a doctoral
program in Chemical Engineering at North Carolina State University.
He recently took an Wiki Scientist course sponsored by the American
Physical Society.</em></p>
<p>My inspiration to become a Wiki Scientist and support unheard
voices through biographies came after reading Brenda Maddox’s
excellent biography of Rosalind Franklin “Rosalind Franklin:
The Dark Lady of DNA” and sadly realizing the long time it
took for the scientific community to give Dr Franklin the due
credit for her ground-breaking work in the discovery of double
helix structure of the DNA.</p>
<p>I believe that by providing scientists from minority and
marginalized communities with their due recognition, we can
reiterate the idea that a scientific contribution can be made
irrespective of sex, race, and religious identity. I was also
motivated to participate in this course because of my personal
belief in promoting open access to credible and vetted scientific
information to public. In the current environment, much of the
technological development is hidden behind expensive archives and
riddled with jargons that are incomprehensible to people without
any field expertise. I strongly believed that education in this
course would teach me how to communicate new scientific information
in a responsible and comprehensive manner to the public.</p>
<p>In my opinion, the time I committed to this course was well
spent as it provided me with an excellent opportunity to highlight
the scientific contributions made by female scientists in the field
of physics and engineering. I was very happy to see the commitment
of Wikipedia users toward disseminating credible information and
maintaining communication (via the ‘Talk’ pages) with
other users in a respectful and professional manner thereby
encouraging informative and thought-provoking discussions.</p>
<p>The course is well-organized and provides all the necessary
information in a succinct format to become a responsible member of
the Wikipedia community. I would like to mention our instructor
Will Kent, who patiently showed us the complex albeit open and
welcoming world of Wikipedia. His feedback on my multiple drafts
helped me publish an article that I am proud of.</p>
<p>I devoted my time toward writing about an Indian physicist,
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shobhana_Narasimhan">Dr
Shobhana Narasimhan,</a> who is currently working at the Jawaharlal
Nehru Centre for Advanced Scientific Research and specializes in
computational nanoscience. It was especially inspiring to research
about her because in addition to being a professor and a successful
researcher, she is also an advocate for increasing women
participation in STEM research and a member of the <em>Standing
committee on Women in Science</em> and <em>National Task force on
Women in Science</em> in India. I was fascinated to read about her
contribution toward developing innovative pedagogical techniques
and her recommendations to the Indian government on promoting
female participation in STEM.</p>
<p>After finishing my PhD, I plan to pursue a career in academia as
a professor, and I strongly believe that this course taught me how
to become an effective and responsible communicator and has
inspired me to contribute toward promotion of diversity and
inclusion in the STEM field. I hope that my testimonial can inspire
other students and members of the STEM community to do the
same.</p>
<p><em>To take a course like the one Yug took, visit <a href="https://wikiedu.org/professional-development/">learn.wikiedu.org</a>.</em></p>
<p><em>Image credit:&nbsp;<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Yug_chandra_saraswat_headshot.jpg">SMR
94</a>, <a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0">CC
BY-SA 4.0</a>, via Wikimedia Commons</em></p>
        </div>
    </div>

    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/phame/live/1/post/259/production_excellence_36_september_2021/">Production Excellence #36: September 2021</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">15:11, Friday, 22 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>How’d we do in our strive for operational excellence last
month? Read on to find out!</p>
<h5 class="remarkup-header">Incidents</h5>
<p>We've had quite an eventful month, with 8 documented incidents
in September. That's the highest since last year (Feb 2020) and one
of the three worst months of the last five years.</p>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-01_partial_parsoid_outage" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-01 partial Parsoid outage</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For 9 hours, 10% of Parsoid
requests to parse/save pages were failing on all wikis. Little to
no end-user impact apart from minor due to RESTBase retries.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-04_appserver_latency" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-04 appserver latency</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For 37 minutes, MW backends
were slow with 2% of requests receiving errors. This affected all
wikis through logged-in users, bots/API queries, and some page
views from unregistered users (e.g. pages that were recently edited
or expired from CDN cache).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-06_Wikifeeds" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-06 Wikifeeds</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For 3 days, the Wikifeeds
API failed ~1% of requests (e.g. 5 of 500 req/s).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-12-Esams-upload" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-12 Esams upload</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For 20 minutes, images were
unavailable for people in Europe, affecting all wikis.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-13_cirrussearch_restart" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-13 CirrusSearch restart</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For ~2 hours, search was
unavailable on Wikipedia from all regions. Search suggestions were
missing or slow, and the search results page errored with "Try
again later".</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-18_appserver_latency" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-18 appserver latency</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For ~10 minutes, MW backends
were slow or unavailable for all wikis.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-26_appserver_latency" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-26 appserver latency</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For ~15 minutes, MW backends
were slow or unavailable for all wikis.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="remarkup-list-item"><a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_documentation/2021-09-29_eqiad-kubernetes" rel="noreferrer">2021-09-29 eqiad kubernetes</a>
<ul class="remarkup-list">
<li class="remarkup-list-item">Impact: For 2 minutes, MW backends
were affected by a Kubernetes issue (via Kask sessionstore). 1500
edit attempts failed (8% of POSTs), and logged-in pageviews were
slowed down, often taking several seconds.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember to review and schedule <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/project/view/4758/" rel="noreferrer">Incident Follow-up work</a> in Phabricator, which are
preventive measures and tech debt mitigations written down after an
incident is concluded.</p>
<div class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-layout-center"><a class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-image" href="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/ggbmdna3pnlmuamch7kp/PHID-FILE-rekdrsz3zeh4p6k5aaqy/proderr-incidents_2021-09.png">
<img alt="proderr-incidents 2021-09.png (830×1 px, 170 KB)" height="300" src="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/ggbmdna3pnlmuamch7kp/PHID-FILE-rekdrsz3zeh4p6k5aaqy/proderr-incidents_2021-09.png" class=" img-responsive"></a></div>
<p>Image from <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://codepen.io/Krinkle/full/wbYMZK" rel="noreferrer">Incident
graphs</a>.</p>
<hr class="remarkup-hr">
<h5 class="remarkup-header"><a name="trends" id="trends"></a>
Trends</h5>
<p>The month of September saw 24 new production error reports of
which 11 have since been resolved, and today, three to six weeks
later, 13 remain open and have thus carried over to the next month.
This is about average, although it makes it no less sad that we
continue to introduce (and carry over) more errors than we rectify
in the same time frame.</p>
<p>On the other hand, last month we did have a healthy focus on
some of the older reports. The workboard stood at 301 unresolved
errors last month. Of those, 16 were resolved. With the 13 new
errors from September, this reduces the total slightly, to 298 open
tasks.</p>
<div class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-layout-center"><a class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-image" href="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/4b455senzns4dbjjbo6q/PHID-FILE-iemr5htdi34vpze4ingd/proderr-unified_2021-09.png">
<img alt="Unresolved error reports, stacked by month." height="400" src="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/4b455senzns4dbjjbo6q/PHID-FILE-iemr5htdi34vpze4ingd/proderr-unified_2021-09.png" class=" img-responsive"></a></div>
<p>For the month-over-month numbers, refer to the <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/e/2PACX-1vTrUCAI10hIroYDU-i5_8s7pony8M71ATXrFRiXXV7t5-tITZYrTRLGch-3iJbmeG41ZMcj1vGfzZ70/pubhtml" rel="noreferrer">spreadsheet data</a>.</p>
<hr class="remarkup-hr">

</ul>

        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://thottingal.in/blog/2021/10/22/one-million-wikipedia-articles/">One million Wikipedia articles by translation</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">06:29, Friday, 22 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>I am happy to share a news from my work at Wikimedia Foundation.
The Wikipedia article translation system, known as Content
Translation reached a milestone of creating one million articles.
Since 2015, this is my major project at WMF and I am lead engineer
for the project. The Content Translation system helps Wikipedia
editors to quickly translate and publish articles from one language
wiki to another. This way, the knowledge gap between different
languages are reduced.</p>
        </div>
    </div>
</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://lu.is/blog/2021/10/21/my-teleconf-setup/">My teleconf setup</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">22:41, Thursday, 21 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>Several friends have asked about my camera/videoconferencing
setup, so some notes on that.</p>
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large is-resized img-responsive"><a href="https://i1.wp.com/lu.is/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/IMG_2261.jpg?ssl=1">
<img alt="" class="wp-image-3892 img-responsive" height="347" src="https://i1.wp.com/lu.is/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/IMG_2261.jpg?resize=521%2C347&amp;ssl=1" width="521"></a>
<figcaption>Picture from my desktop camera. Lighting isn’t
quite as even as I’d like (and as always in stills, my smile
is goofy) but you can see the background blur clearly.</figcaption>
</figure>
<h2>Why?</h2>
<p>I’ve joked that for lawyers, a good videoconferencing
setup is now like a good suit—sort of pointless but
nevertheless can help make a good impression in a field where
impressions, for better and for worse, matter.</p>
<p>I picked up the new book “<a href="https://www.duarte.com/presenting-virtually/">Presenting
Virtually</a>” from Duarte and it starts with something
that’s pretty basic, but also not always obvious—you
can’t control networks, and often don’t control what
presentation software you’re using. What you do control is
your hardware, so make that the best you can.</p>
<h2>Camera</h2>
<p>I bought a <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Canon-1892C001-EOS-77D-Body/dp/B06VSTCWJ9?th=1">
Canon 77D</a> to take baby pictures and… it was in a closet
when the pandemic hit. I use it with a <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Canon-EF-S-24mm-2-8-Lens/dp/B00NI3BZ5K/ref=sr_1_3?dchild=1&amp;keywords=ef-s+24mm+f%2F2.8+stm+lens&amp;qid=1634842704&amp;s=electronics&amp;sr=1-3">
24mm pancake lens</a>. Canon provides a <a href="https://www.usa.canon.com/internet/portal/us/home/support/self-help-center/eos-webcam-utility">
driver</a> that lets you use the camera as a webcam.</p>
<p>Given the cost, I’m not sure this makes sense for most
people to do unless they already have a compatible Canon laying
around. But if you do have a supported one it works great!</p>
<p>As an alternative, friends speak very highly of <a href="https://www.dell.com/en-us/shop/dell-ultrasharp-webcam/apd/319-bbhp/pc-accessories">
this new Dell camera</a>.</p>
<h2>Light</h2>
<p>I cheat by having good natural light in my office and then
supplementing it, rather than having to blast light all over to
make up for the gap. This means my light was cheap; the primary
criteria was being able to change the color (from a bright white to
yellow-ish) so that things looked right.</p>
<p>The exact model I got is no longer available, but is basically
<a href="https://www.amazon.com/Desktop-Seamless-Brightness-Temperature-Charging/dp/B00LZPB7OC/ref=sxin_23?asc_contentid=amzn1.osa.37300557-036a-4bbf-9c4a-2bbd5e7248c1.ATVPDKIKX0DER.en_US&amp;asc_contenttype=article&amp;ascsubtag=amzn1.osa.37300557-036a-4bbf-9c4a-2bbd5e7248c1.ATVPDKIKX0DER.en_US&amp;creativeASIN=B00LZPB7OC&amp;cv_ct_cx=taotronics+led+desk+lamp&amp;cv_ct_id=amzn1.osa.37300557-036a-4bbf-9c4a-2bbd5e7248c1.ATVPDKIKX0DER.en_US&amp;cv_ct_pg=search&amp;cv_ct_we=asin&amp;cv_ct_wn=osp-single-source-earns-comm&amp;dchild=1&amp;keywords=taotronics+led+desk+lamp&amp;linkCode=oas&amp;pd_rd_i=B00LZPB7OC&amp;pd_rd_r=7cc6bf0c-3887-4e6c-a680-5f7353eabd5f&amp;pd_rd_w=PT12E&amp;pd_rd_wg=KkEPe&amp;pf_rd_p=5846ecd6-3f37-4a28-8efc-9c817c03dbe9&amp;pf_rd_r=5MMVS0FPHGRGFR4ECE7S&amp;qid=1634853112&amp;sr=1-4-64f3a41a-73ca-403a-923c-8152c45485fe&amp;tag=bestcont06-20">
similar to this one</a>.</p>
<p>Pro tip for new-ish home workers: if you have two rooms, one
dark and one bright, make your bedroom dark and cramped and your
office big and light. The previous residents of our place made the
reverse choice and I don’t understand it at all.</p>
<h2>Microphone</h2>
<p>I have <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07DTTGZ7M/r">a Blue Yeti
mic</a>. I’m not sure I’d recommend it for most people.
The audio quality is very good, but positioning it over a desk is
finicky. (I use <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07CTFZSXZ/">these</a> for both
my camera and mic, and they work once you get them set up, but
they’re a pain.) In addition, it has a headphone
jack—which is fine except it insists on reporting to the
operating system that it is live even when it has nothing plugged
in, so I frequently have to say “no, bad zoom, use the
speakers that are actually speakers”.</p>
<p>If I were doing it over again, I’d get something designed
more specifically for the home office use case. A friend swears by
<a href="https://www.jabra.com/Business/speakerphones/jabra-speak-series/jabra-speak-510">
their Jabra 510</a>, and this <a href="https://www.logitech.com/en-us/products/personal-workspaces/logi-dock.html">
new thing from Logitech</a> looks pretty interesting.</p>
<h2>What I’m not doing (at least not yet)</h2>
<p>I’m sorely tempted to get a teleprompter, but <a href="https://redmonk.com/sogrady/2021/04/23/fancy-camera-rig/">Stephen
has mostly convinced me not to</a>. In my experience, at this time,
the bar is pretty low—having a good camera and light really
does make things noticeably better for people on the other end,
even if your eye contact isn’t perfect while doing a slide
deck. So you can get a lot of bang for a lot less effort than
Stephen spent. Still, tempting some days :)</p>
<p>Hope this is helpful!</p>
        </div>
    </div>

            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/phame/live/1/post/248/production_excellence_35_august_2021/">Production Excellence #35: August 2021</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">23:01, Wednesday, 20 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>How’d we do in our strive for operational excellence last
month? Read on to find out!</p>
<h5 class="remarkup-header">Incidents</h5>
<p>Zero documented incidents last month. Isn't that something!</p>
<p>Learn about past incidents at <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Incident_status" rel="noreferrer">Incident status</a> on Wikitech. Remember to review
and schedule <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/project/view/4758/" rel="noreferrer">Incident Follow-up</a> in Phabricator, which are
preventive measures and other action items to learn from.</p>
<div class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-layout-center"><a class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-image" href="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/ggfsx3vumi7uvqbxqcxd/PHID-FILE-kbgcqy7wy3joaitvfw45/proderr-incidents_2021-08.png">
<img alt="proderr-incidents 2021-08.png (834×2 px, 288 KB)" height="278" src="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/ggfsx3vumi7uvqbxqcxd/PHID-FILE-kbgcqy7wy3joaitvfw45/proderr-incidents_2021-08.png" class=" img-responsive"></a></div>
<p>Image from <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://codepen.io/Krinkle/full/wbYMZK" rel="noreferrer">Incident
graphs</a>.</p>
<hr class="remarkup-hr">
<h5 class="remarkup-header"><a name="trends" id="trends"></a>
Trends</h5>
<p>In August we resolved 18 of the 156 reports that carried over
from previous months, and reported 46 new failures in production.
Of the new ones, 17 remain unresolved as of writing and will carry
over to next month.</p>
<p>The number of new errors reports in August was fairly high at
46, compared to 31 reports in July, and 26 reports in June.</p>
<div class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-layout-center"><a class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-image" href="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/2eb2dyaxn4w4gs46hpjj/PHID-FILE-2hbqmdnpgj342nftwuhe/proderr-monthly_2021-09-03.png">
<img alt="Unresolved error reports, stacked by month" height="300" src="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/2eb2dyaxn4w4gs46hpjj/PHID-FILE-2hbqmdnpgj342nftwuhe/proderr-monthly_2021-09-03.png" class=" img-responsive"></a></div>
<p>The backlog of "Old" issues saw no progress this past month and
remained constant at 146 open error reports.</p>
<div class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-layout-center"><a class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-image" href="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/y5sc5xhvko2sjc6v4wt7/PHID-FILE-7qkcf2tqicd2fvo3zqco/proderr-totals_2021-09-03.png">
<img alt="Total open production error tasks, by month." height="300" src="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/y5sc5xhvko2sjc6v4wt7/PHID-FILE-7qkcf2tqicd2fvo3zqco/proderr-totals_2021-09-03.png" class=" img-responsive"></a></div>
<p>Unified graph:<br></p>
<div class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-layout-center"><a class="phabricator-remarkup-embed-image" href="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/qs2palfu5jyddm3tbhw2/PHID-FILE-nzvqzkd4264qk6w5asha/proderr-unified_2021-08.png">
<img alt="proderr-unified 2021-08.png (1×1 px, 78 KB)" height="400" src="https://phab.wmfusercontent.org/file/data/qs2palfu5jyddm3tbhw2/PHID-FILE-nzvqzkd4264qk6w5asha/proderr-unified_2021-08.png" class=" img-responsive"></a></div>
<blockquote class="remarkup-reply-block">
<div class="remarkup-reply-head">💡 <strong>Did you
know</strong>:</div>
<div class="remarkup-reply-body">
<p>You can zoom in to your team's error reports by using the
appropriate "Filter" link in the sidebar of our shared <a class="remarkup-link" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/tag/wikimedia-production-error/" rel="noreferrer">workboard</a>.</p>
</div>
</blockquote>
<p>Take a look at the workboard and look for tasks that could use
your help.</p>
<p><span class="remarkup-nav-sequence"><a class="phui-tag-view phui-tag-type-shade phui-tag-grey phui-tag-shade phui-tag-icon-view" href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/tag/wikimedia-production-error/" rel="noreferrer" target="_blank"><span class="phui-tag-core">View
Workboard</span></a></span></p>

    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://wikiedu.org/blog/2021/10/20/fly-little-item-and-be-useful-to-someone/">“Fly, little item, and be useful to someone!”</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">16:39, Wednesday, 20 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <figure class="wp-caption alignright img-responsive" id="attachment_41433" style="width: 400px;"><img alt="Julia Novakovic head shot" class="size-full wp-image-41433 img-responsive" height="400" src="https://wikiedu.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/Julia-Novakovic.jpg" width="400">
<figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-41433">
Julia Novakovic</figcaption>
</figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">At a conference a few years ago,
Julia Novakovic got inspired by the idea of linked data. As an
Archivist for the</span> <a href="https://www.museumofplay.org/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Strong National Museum of Play</span></a>
<span style="font-weight: 400;">in Rochester, New York, Julia is
responsible for the preservation of, and providing access to,
primary source documentation relating to the study of play,
artifacts of play, and video and electronic game history. So when
an opportunity came her way to join one of Wiki
Education’s</span> <a href="http://wikiedu.org/wikidata"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Wikidata Institute</span></a> <span style="font-weight: 400;">courses through the New York Data Carpentries
Library Consortium (NYDCLC), Julia remembered her earlier dreams of
linked data — and set out making them a reality.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“The</span> <a href="https://www.museumofplay.org/collections/icheg/women-in-games-initiative/">
<span style="font-weight: 400;">Women in Games
Initiative</span></a> <span style="font-weight: 400;">at The Strong
shares the ever-evolving story of women’s contributions to
the video game industry, and I thought that using linked data to
map this initiative would be a very useful resource,” she
says. “If we could create a visualization showing that this
woman worked for X company, which also employed this woman, who
collaborated with this other woman, and so on, it could really show
impact on, and growth of, the video game industry. We could then
also link people to related collections materials—whether
museum objects (like games or hardware), or archival collections
(like</span> <a href="http://archives.museumofplay.org/subjects/612"><span style="font-weight: 400;">primary source documentation</span></a>
<span style="font-weight: 400;">or</span> <a href="https://museumofplay.access.preservica.com/uncategorized/SO_45768521-ffa7-490a-a03e-cbe7c871d0b1/">
<span style="font-weight: 400;">oral history
interviews</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">). While
I’ve since been preoccupied with other duties and projects at
The Strong, I realized that getting involved with Wikidata might
just be the boost I need to learn more and be able to see this idea
come to fruition.”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Wiki Education’s Wikidata
Institute course provided that boost for Julia. Through
twice-weekly Zoom sessions for three weeks led by Will Kent, out of
class online tutorials, and a plethora of tools and visualizations
to explore, Julia quickly became immersed in the world of Wikidata.
And because she was part of a cohort of fellow NYDCLC participants,
Julia got even more out of the course.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“It was actually pretty
useful for me to have classmates in the same region because we had
a lot of topics and questions in common,” she says. “I
had also met a handful of them in person at previous events or
conferences too, and it was nice to see familiar
faces!”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">As part of the course, she added
references to items in Wikidata related to her areas of expertise
at the museum. This led her down the Wikidata wormhole of creating
items for publications, then linking those items as a reference for
another item. She spent some time on the Monopoly article, as The
Strong’s archives have lots of materials related to the
Parker Brothers games.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“My favorite part is the
satisfaction that accompanies a new item going out into the
ether,” Julia says. “Fly, little item, and be useful to
someone!”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Since the class wrapped up, she
has connected with colleagues at the museum to do more work on
Wikidata items related to an upcoming Women in Games celebration.
And she’s planning to incorporate Wikidata into a new website
her museum recently launched, the</span> <a href="https://sacksonportal.museumofplay.org/s/sackson-portal/page/welcome">
<span style="font-weight: 400;">Sid Sackson
Portal</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Julia encourages more librarians
and archivists to contribute to Wikidata</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“As information
professionals, it should be second nature for us to want to help
make data out there better,” she says, “whether
that’s by creating items, making edits when needed, or
providing references for users.”</span></p>
<p><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">The New York Data Carpentries
Library Consortium sponsored this course for librarians in Western
and Central New York, thanks to financial support from the
Institute of Museum and Library Services. To bring together
librarians, data professionals, and others at your institution for
a similar learning experience, contact
partner@wikiedu.org.</span></i></p>
<p><em>Image credits:&nbsp;<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Strong4625.JPG">עדירל</a>,
<a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0">CC BY-SA
4.0</a>, via Wikimedia Commons; <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Julia_Novakovic.jpg">Jnovakovic09</a>,
<a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0">CC BY-SA
4.0</a>, via Wikimedia Commons</em></p>
        </div>
    </div>
</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://techblog.wikimedia.org/2021/10/19/iterating-on-how-we-do-nfs-at-wikimedia-cloud-services/">Iterating on how we do NFS at Wikimedia Cloud Services</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">19:27, Tuesday, 19 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <h4>By Arturo Borrero González, Site Reliability Engineer,
Wikimedia Cloud Services Team</h4>
<h2>The current situation</h2>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_File_System">NFS</a> is a
central piece of technology for some of the services that the
<a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Help:Cloud_Services_Introduction">
Wikimedia Cloud Services</a> team offers to the community. We have
several shares that power different use cases: <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Portal:Toolforge">Toolforge</a>
user home directories live on NFS, and <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Portal:Cloud_VPS">Cloud
VPS</a> users can also access <a href="https://dumps.wikimedia.org/">dumps</a> using this protocol. The
current setup involves several physical hardware servers, with
about 20TB of storage, offering shares over 10G links to the cloud.
For the system to be more fault-tolerant, we duplicate each share
for redundancy using <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_Replicated_Block_Device">
DRBD</a>.<br></p>
<p>Running NFS on dedicated hardware servers has traditionally
offered us advantages: mostly on the performance and the capacity
fields.</p>
<p>As time has passed, we have been enumerating more and more
reasons to review how we do NFS. For one, the current setup is in
violation of some of <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Cross-Realm_traffic_guidelines">
our internal rules regarding realm separation</a>. Additionally, we
had been longing for additional flexibility managing our servers:
we wanted to use virtual machines managed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenStack">Openstack</a> Nova. The
DRBD-based high-availability system required mostly a hand-crafted
procedure for failover/failback. There’s also some
scalability concerns as NFS is easy to grow up, but not to grow
horizontally, and of course, we have to be able to keep the tenancy
setup while doing so, something that NFS does by using LDAP/Unix
users and may get complicated too when growing. In general, the
servers have become ‘too big to fail’, clearly
technical debt, and it has taken us years to decide on taking on
the task to rethink the architecture. It’s worth mentioning
that in an ideal world, we wouldn’t depend on NFS, but the
truth is that it will still be a central piece of infrastructure
for years to come in services like Toolforge.</p>
<p>Over a series of brainstorming meetings, the WMCS team evaluated
the situation and sorted out the many moving parts. The team&nbsp;
managed to boil down the potential service future to two competing
options:</p>
<ul>
<li>Adopt and introduce a new Openstack component into our cloud:
<a href="https://www.openstack.org/software/releases/xena/components/manila">
Manila</a> — this was the right choice if we were interested
in a general <em>NFS as a service</em> offering for our Cloud VPS
users.</li>
<li>Put the data on <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Help:Adding_Disk_Space_to_Cloud_VPS_instances#Cinder:_Attachable_Block_Storage_for_Cloud_VPS">
Cinder</a> volumes and serve NFS from a couple of virtual machines
created by hand — this was the right choice if we wanted
something that required low effort to engineer and adopt.</li>
</ul>
<p>Then we decided to research both options in parallel. For a
number of reasons, the evaluation was timeboxed to three weeks.
Both ideas had a couple of points in common: the NFS data would be
stored on our <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Portal:Cloud_VPS/Admin/Ceph">Ceph</a>
farm via Cinder volumes, and we would rely on Ceph reliability to
avoid using DRBD. Another open topic was how to back up data from
Ceph, to store our important bits in more than one basket. We will
get to the back up topic later.</p>
<h2>The manila experiment</h2>
<p>The Wikimedia Foundation was an early adopter of some Openstack
components (<a href="https://docs.openstack.org/nova/latest/">Nova</a>, <a href="https://docs.openstack.org/glance/latest/">Glance</a>, <a href="https://docs.openstack.org/designate/latest/">Designate</a>,
<a href="https://docs.openstack.org/horizon/latest/">Horizon</a>),
but <a href="https://wiki.openstack.org/wiki/Manila">Manila</a> was
never evaluated for usage until now. Our approach for this
experiment was to closely follow the upstream guidelines. We read
the documentation and tried to understand the different setups you
can build with Manila. As we often feel with other Openstack
components, the documentation doesn’t perfectly describe how
to introduce a given component in your particular local setup. Here
we use an admin-controller flat-topology Neutron network. This
network is shared by all tenants (or projects) in our Openstack
deployment. Also, Manila can use many <a href="https://docs.openstack.org/manila/latest/configuration/shared-file-systems/drivers.html">
different driver backends</a>, for things like NetApps or
CephFS—that we don’t use…, yet. After some
research, the <a href="https://docs.openstack.org/manila/latest/configuration/shared-file-systems/drivers/generic-driver.html">
generic driver</a> was the one that seemed to better fit our use
case. The generic driver leverages Nova virtual machines instances
plus Cinder volume to create and manage the shares. In general,
Manila supports two operational modes, whether it should
create/destroy the share servers (i.e, the virtual machine
instances) or not. This option is called
<em>driver_handles_share_server</em> (or <a href="https://docs.openstack.org/manila/xena/admin/shared-file-systems-share-types.html">
DHSS</a>) and takes a boolean value.&nbsp;</p>
<p>We were interested in trying with <strong>DHSS=true</strong>, to
really benefit from the potential of the setup.</p>
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large img-responsive"><a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:NFS-idea_6(1).png"><img alt="" class="wp-image-1732 img-responsive" height="869" src="https://techblog.wikimedia.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/image.png?w=1000" width="1600"></a>
<figcaption><a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:NFS-idea_6(1).png" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:NFS-idea_6(1).png</a>,
By Arturo Borrero González, <a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0/">CC-BY-SA
4.0</a></figcaption>
</figure>
<p>So, after sorting all these variables, we moved on with our
initial testing. We built a PoC setup as depicted in the diagram
above, with the manila-share component running in a virtual machine
inside the cloud. The PoC led to us reporting several bugs
upstream:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://bugs.launchpad.net/manila/+bug/1946002">#1946002 generic
driver: service instance ends up with 2 ports in the admin
network</a></li>
<li><a href="https://bugs.launchpad.net/manila/+bug/1945463">#1945463 generic
driver: service instance name template is ignored</a></li>
<li><a href="https://bugs.launchpad.net/manila/+bug/1944980">#1944980 generic
driver: support additional SSH options for service
instance</a></li>
<li><a href="https://bugs.launchpad.net/manila/+bug/1944696">#1944696 [DOC]
document additional generic driver configuration options</a></li>
</ul>
<p>In some cases we tried to address these bugs ourselves:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://review.opendev.org/c/openstack/manila/+/810702">https://review.opendev.org/c/openstack/manila/+/810702</a></li>
<li><a href="https://review.opendev.org/c/openstack/manila/+/810719">https://review.opendev.org/c/openstack/manila/+/810719</a></li>
<li><a href="https://review.opendev.org/c/openstack/manila/+/811736">https://review.opendev.org/c/openstack/manila/+/811736</a></li>
</ul>
<p>It’s worth mentioning that the upstream community was
extra-welcoming to us, and we’re thankful for that. However,
at the end of our three-week period, our Manila setup still
wasn’t working as expected. Your experience may change with
other drivers—perhaps the ZFSonLinux or the CephFS ones. In
general, we were having trouble making the setup work as expected,
so we decided to abandon this approach in favor of the other option
we were considering at the beginning.</p>
<h2>Simple virtual machine serving NFS</h2>
<p>The alternative was to create a Nova virtual machine instance by
hand and to configure it using puppet. We have been investing in an
<a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Spicerack">automation
framework</a> lately, so the idea is to not actually create the
server by hand. Anyway, the data would be decoupled from the
instance into Cinder volumes, which led us to the question we left
for later: How should we back up those terabytes of important
information? Just to be clear, the backup problem was independent
of the above options; with Manila we would still have had to solve
the same challenge. We would like to see our data be backed up
somewhere else other than in Ceph. And that’s exactly where
we are at right now. We’ve been exploring <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Cloud_Services_team/EnhancementProposals/cinder_backups">
different backup strategies</a> and will finally use the Cinder
backup API.</p>
<h2>Conclusion</h2>
<p>The iteration will end with the dedicated NFS hardware servers
being stopped, and the shares being served from within the cloud.
The migration will take some time to happen because we will check
and double-check that everything works as expected (including from
the performance point of view) before making definitive changes. We
already have some plans to make sure our users experience as little
service impact as possible. The most troublesome shares will be
those related to Toolforge. At some point we will need to disallow
writes to the NFS share, rsync the data out of the hardware servers
into the Cinder volumes, point the NFS clients to the new virtual
machines, and then enable writes again. The main Toolforge share
has about 8TB of data, so this will take a while.</p>
<p>We will have more updates in the future. Who knows, perhaps our
next-next iteration, in a couple of years, will see us adopting
Openstack Manila for good.</p>
<h2>About this post</h2>
<p><em><strong>Featured image credit:</strong></em> <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:(from_break_water)_Manila_Skyline_-_panoramio.jpg">
File:(from break water) Manila Skyline – panoramio.jpg</a>,
<a href="http://www.panoramio.com/user/2912147?with_photo_id=19568662">ewol</a>,
<a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/deed.en">CC
BY-SA 3.0</a></p>
        </div>
    </div>
</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://wikiedu.org/blog/2021/10/18/the-wiki-education-wow-moments/">The Wiki Education Wow Moments</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">16:06, Monday, 18 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p><em>Jay. F Bolin is an Associate Professor and Chair of the
Biology Department at Catawba College, Salisbury, North
Carolina.</em></p>
<figure class="wp-caption alignright img-responsive" id="attachment_41346" style="width: 300px;"><img alt="Jay Bolin head shot" class="wp-image-41346 size-full img-responsive" height="400" src="https://wikiedu.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/Bolin-Headshot.jpg" width="300">
<figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-41346">
Jay Bolin Image courtesy Jay Bolin, all rights
reserved.</figcaption>
</figure>
<p>As a college professor I’m fortunate to teach subjects I
love at Catawba College and teaching with Wiki Education I can
confidently say has made my teaching even more satisfying. Since
2016, I’ve used Wiki Education in three Plant Taxonomy
courses (one that I’m offering this fall) and one Dendrology
Course (for those not into esoteric -ologies, that’s a course
on the biology of trees). I’ll admit I was not a Wikipedia
editor before learning about Wiki Education at a scientific
conference and still haven’t been fully transformed into a
late night Wikipedian. But, I do dabble on occasion, since
I’ve been learning about editing Wikipedia right along with
my students.</p>
<p>In my courses where I employ Wiki Education the implementation
is incredibly straightforward, I have students find stubs (sad
nubbins of Wikipedia pages) for native plants in my home state of
North Carolina. With over 4,000 plants in the Tar Heel state, the
student’s task of finding a stub for a plant that is
interesting to them and developing a reasonable Wikipedia species
page is a challenging but still reasonable ask. They explore and
write succinct and dispassionate descriptions in Wikipedia of the
plants themselves, their ecology, taxonomy, and any other area that
the students choose with adequate references. I love the
self-directed aspect of Wiki Education assignments; for example, if
a student is interested in Native American uses of a plant they
follow that path, if they are biochemistry nuts they can describe
medicinally active compounds.</p>
<p><img alt="screenshot of iMessage conversation" class="alignright wp-image-41345 img-responsive" height="371" src="https://wikiedu.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/IMG_3632.jpg" width="444">Mince no words, implementing Wiki Education in your
classroom is work, but it is rewarding for so many reasons. Just
this week, I was on a nerdy iMessage thread with two other academic
botanists about the identification of a particular maple tree in
Kentucky. We were discussing possible options then when I intuited
that he was reading from a Wikipedia page that my student primarily
authored! There aren’t a lot of student assignments that you
work on with your student and spend time carefully editing that
make an impact like Wiki Education outside of the classroom. Just
so you know, the popular “facepalm” emoticon on the
right is more of a mind-blown happy thing than the traditional
usage.</p>
<p>Another “Ah-Ha” or Wow teaching moment that I had a
few years ago was in a Plant Taxonomy Class. While students were
doing some revisions and research on their own Wikipedia plant
species pages in class, a student just yelled out “NOOOOOO,
NOOOOOOOO” and gesticulated wildly, alarmed I walked over and
asked what the issue was. He shook his head and showed me his
phone. He had the astute idea of doing more research on his focal
plant species using a very widely used photo identification phone
app called iNaturalist. &nbsp;When he pulled up the description of
the plant species in iNaturalist, what he saw was his own writing,
talk about circular: He had written nearly all of the Wikipedia
page, already made it “live” and was looking for
guidance from his own writing. As many natural historians know
Wikipedia is an invaluable source of freely available taxonomic
information, &nbsp;iNaturalist (funded by the California Academy of
Science and National Geographic) and the Encyclopedia of Life
(funded by the Smithsonian Institution) both feed some or all of
their descriptive data from Wikipedia. Soon all the students
whipped out their phones (OK I’m lying they were already out
on the lab tables), and looked up their focal Wiki Education
species on the iNaturalist app, and were one by one blown away and
shaken, that the inviolable fount of knowledge, their phones, were
linking their own writing, for class! After that they realized that
they were the experts and took their tasks of editing and
researching “their plant pages” with solemn
seriousness.</p>
<p>A few protips from a somewhat seasoned Wiki Education professor
(78.K words &amp; 926 references added by students and an astounding
611k plant species page views! (this is how Wikipedians talk)): If
you aren’t using Wiki Education in the classroom I suggest
giving it a whirl, as long as 1) your class is relatively small, 2)
your students are mostly Junior or Seniors, and 3) you have time (I
know) to edit your student’s short Wikipedia entries. As a
final thought, if you are preparing a new course, <em>that</em>
would be a good time to introduce a Wiki Education assignment.
Mashing the well thought out Wiki Education training and modules
into an existing course may not work unless you can take a paring
knife to the precious content you have developed for a course that
you’ve taught a few times. I enjoy teaching with Wiki
Education and I think you will too.</p>
<p><em>Image credit:&nbsp;<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Catawba_College_2.jpg">Kharris0317</a>,
<a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0">CC BY-SA
4.0</a>, via Wikimedia Commons</em></p>
        </div>
    </div>

<div class="plainlinks">
<p>Latest <b><a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News" title="m:Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News">tech news</a></b> from the
Wikimedia technical community. Please tell other users about these
changes. Not all changes will affect you. <a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News/2021/42" title="m:Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News/2021/42">Translations</a> are
available.</p>
<p><b>Recent changes</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Toolhub" title="m:Toolhub">Toolhub</a> is a catalogue to make it easier to
find software tools that can be used for working on the Wikimedia
projects. You can <a class="external text" href="https://lists.wikimedia.org/hyperkitty/list/wikitech-l@lists.wikimedia.org/thread/LF4SSR4QRCKV6NPRFGUAQWUFQISVIPTS/">
read more</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Changes later this week</b></p>
<ul>
<li><img alt="Recurrent item" height="16" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Octicons-sync.svg/12px-Octicons-sync.svg.png" title="Recurrent item" width="12" class=" img-responsive"> The <a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/MediaWiki_1.38/wmf.5" title="mw:MediaWiki 1.38/wmf.5">new version</a> of MediaWiki will be on
test wikis and MediaWiki.org from 19 October. It will be on
non-Wikipedia wikis and some Wikipedias from 20 October. It will be
on all wikis from 21 October (<a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/MediaWiki_1.38/Roadmap" title="mw:MediaWiki 1.38/Roadmap">calendar</a>).</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Future changes</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The developers of the <a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Apps/Team/Android" title="mw:Wikimedia Apps/Team/Android">Wikipedia Android app</a> are
working on <a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Apps/Team/Android/Communication" title="mw:Wikimedia Apps/Team/Android/Communication">communication
in the app</a>. You can now answer questions in <a class="extiw" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Apps/Team/Android/Communication/UsertestingOctober2021" title="mw:Wikimedia Apps/Team/Android/Communication/UsertestingOctober2021">
survey</a> to help the development.</li>
<li>3–5% of editors may be blocked in the next few months.
This is because of a new service in Safari, which is similar to a
<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/en:Proxy_server" title="w:en:Proxy server">proxy</a> or a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/en:VPN" title="w:en:VPN">VPN</a>. It
is called iCloud Private Relay. There is a <a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Apple_iCloud_Private_Relay" title="m:Special:MyLanguage/Apple iCloud Private Relay">discussion
about this</a> on Meta. The goal is to learn what iCloud Private
Relay could mean for the communities.</li>
<li><a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Wikimedia_Enterprise" title="m:Special:MyLanguage/Wikimedia Enterprise">Wikimedia
Enterprise</a> is a new <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/en:API" title="w:en:API">API</a> for
those who use a lot of information from the Wikimedia projects on
other sites. It is a way to get big commercial users to pay for the
data. There will soon be a copy of the Wikimedia Enterprise
dataset. You can <a class="external text" href="https://lists.wikimedia.org/hyperkitty/list/wikitech-ambassadors@lists.wikimedia.org/message/B2AX6PWH5MBKB4L63NFZY3ADBQG7MSBA/">
read more</a>. You can also ask the team questions <a class="external text" href="https://wikimedia.zoom.us/j/88994018553" rel="nofollow">on Zoom</a> on <a class="external text" href="https://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/fixedtime.html?hour=15&amp;min=00&amp;sec=0&amp;day=22&amp;month=10&amp;year=2021" rel="nofollow">22 October 15:00 UTC</a>.</li>
</ul>

by <a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News/Writers" title="m:Special:MyLanguage/Tech/News/Writers">Tech News
