    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://weeklyosm.eu/archives/14912">weeklyOSM 586</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">10:33, Sunday, 17 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <p>05/10/2021-11/10/2021</p>
<div class="wp-caption alignnone img-responsive" style="width: 1010px;">
<p class="wp-caption-text"><img alt="lead picture" height="478" src="https://i0.wp.com/weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2021/10/586_T_all.png?resize=719%2C478&amp;ssl=1" width="719" class=" img-responsive"></p>
<p class="wp-caption-text"><a href="https://gitlab.com/dsantini/open-etymology-map/-/blob/main/CONTRIBUTING.md">
Daniele Santini</a>‘s Open Etymology Map [<a href="https://weeklyosm.eu/feed#wn586_25683"><sup>1</sup></a>] ©
<a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q80992">Wikidata</a>,
<a href="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/Coat_of_arms_of_the_House_of_Sforza.svg">
Wikimedia Commons</a>, Mapbox | map data © <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/copyright">OpenStreetMap
contributors</a></p>
</div>
<h2 id="wn586_mapping">Mapping</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25696">Daniel Capilla <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/dcapillae/diary/397798">told</a>
<img alt="(es)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/es.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/dcapillae/diary/397798">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> us in his blog that the reality in Malaga has nothing to do
with the old cliché ‘Malaga, city of a thousand bars and
only one bookshop’, sharing details related to bookshop and
libraries mapped in OSM.</li>
<li id="wn586_25680">Voting is underway for <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Proposed_features/boundary%3Dborder_zone">
<code>boundary=border_zone</code></a>, for tagging areas near
borders that have special restrictions on movement (till Friday 22
October).</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_community">Community</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25719">The <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Unite_Maps_Initiative/UN_Mappers">
UN Mappers</a> Crowdsourcing Team <a href="https://twitter.com/UN_Mappers/status/1447820553621057536">organised</a>
its first online training in Portuguese. The activity was in
collaboration with the Munzuá Research Group from <a href="https://unilab.edu.br/">UNILAB</a> <img alt="(pt)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/pt.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://unilab.edu.br/">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a>. Over six sessions of three hours each, the aim was to both
train new contributors on OSM mapping and provide insights
regarding the OSM ecosystem. The overall objective is to support
the development of OSM communities in Portuguese-speaking countries
in Africa. In addition, the <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Highway_Tag_Africa">Highway
tag Africa</a> OSM wiki page has been translated into
Portuguese.</li>
<li id="wn586_25687">The University of the Philippines’ NOAH
(Nationwide Operational Assessment of Hazards) has formally
<a href="https://noah.up.edu.ph/">launched</a> its revamped
website, which uses OpenStreetMap datasets to identify hazard
exposure and risk for the whole country.</li>
<li id="wn586_25695">After only one week as a mapper in the OSM
world Sebastian Helm <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/SebastianHelm/diary/397797">wrote</a>
a blog post about his first impressions of mapping and pointed out
some aspects that, from his point of view, make it difficult for
new mappers to stay on the ball.</li>
<li id="wn586_25684">Simon Poole <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/SimonPoole/diary/397810">shared</a>
that he sent the 10,000<sup>th</sup> new contributor a welcome
message on Tuesday 5 October. The first was sent in December
2013.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_openstreetmap_foundation">OpenStreetMap
Foundation</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25708">Dorothea Kazazi <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/osmf-talk/2021-October/008153.html">
released</a> three reports highlighting recent updates related to
the OSMF, including local chapter news and membership
statistics.</li>
<li id="wn586_25709">Amanda McCann <a href="https://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/osmf-talk/2021-October/008139.html">
suggested</a>, on the OSMF-Talk mailing list, that the State of the
Map brand should not be used for events in places where
homosexuality is banned and persecuted.</li>
<li id="wn586_25693">The minutes of the Friday 24 September OSMF
Board meeting have been <a href="https://wiki.osmfoundation.org/wiki/Board/Minutes/2021-09">released</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_local_chapter_news">Local chapter news</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25697">Christian Quest <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/cquest/diary/397813">wrote</a>
<img alt="(fr)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/fr.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/cquest/diary/397813">
<img alt="de" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> about the creation of OpenStreetMap France on the occasion of
its 10<sup>th</sup> birthday.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_events">Events</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25689">Pista ng Mapa (Festival of Maps) is an annual
open and geo conference held in the Philippines. Registration is
<a href="https://pistangmapa.github.io/2021/">open</a> until Sunday
31 October.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_education">Education</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25706">In this tutorial Amanda McCann <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4Zt7MJChM2o">demonstrates</a>
using different GPS positions for mapping, creating curved and
unusually shaped buildings, and the all-important terrace.</li>
<li id="wn586_25698">Amelia Hunt and Doug Specht, academics at
University of Westminster (London ), <a href="https://jhumanitarianaction.springeropen.com/articles/10.1186/s41018-018-0048-1">
published</a> ‘Crowdsurced mapping in crisis zones:
collaboration, organisation and impact’, in the <em>Journal
of International Humanitarian Action</em>. The paper presents case
studies centred on crowdsourcing communities, such as the <a href="https://standbytaskforce.wordpress.com/">Standby Task Force</a>
(SBTF), which activate on a case-by-case basis at the request of
international agencies and/or local actors. These communities
gather and analyse, in real time, social media information during
conflict and disaster, and produce POI maps.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_humanitarian_osm">Humanitarian OSM</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25686">HOT Open Mapping Hub – Asia Pacific
<a href="https://www.hotosm.org/updates/announcing-booster-for-communities-and-organizations-in-the-asia-pacific/">
announced</a> their Booster Grant programme – OpenStreetMap
community/ecosystem investments in Bangladesh, Nepal and the
Philippines.</li>
<li id="wn586_25685">At HOT’s Annual General Meeting (held on
7 October), the HOT Voting Membership <a href="https://www.hotosm.org/updates/board-election-results-from-the-2021-annual-meeting/">
elected</a> five members to the Board of Directors. Chad Blevins
replaces Matt Gibb as the newly elected Voting Membership
Chairperson. Four amendments to the organisation’s by-laws
were also approved.</li>
<li id="wn586_25688">Outgoing HOT Board President, Miriam
Mapanauta, <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/Mapanauta/diary/397808">shared</a>
her End of Term Report 2019–2021.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_maps">Maps</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25683"><a href="https://www.dsantini.it/etymology/">Open Etymology Map</a> shows
the etymology of names based on OSM and Wikidata.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_licences">Licences</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25694">LySioS <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/LySioS/diary/397785">wondered</a>
if the OSM copyright notice might not be better clarified by a
word-picture mark rather than plain text to indicate OSM’s
contribution. Various people in the thread pointed to earlier
discussions on the theme.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_software">Software</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25699">Geofabrik <a href="https://twitter.com/geofabrik/status/1446414179808825358?s=20">tweeted</a>
that their <a href="http://tools.geofabrik.de/osmi/">OSM
Inspector</a> QA tool is now being updated twice a day.</li>
<li id="wn586_25676">Pieter Vander Vennet released a new version of
<a href="https://mapcomplete.osm.be/">MapComplete</a>. As <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/Pieter%20Vander%20Vennet/diary/397796">
detailed</a> in his diary entry, it contains a heap of new themes
(for example, <a href="https://mapcomplete.osm.be/charging_stations.html">charging
stations</a>, <a href="https://mapcomplete.osm.be/cafes_and_pubs.html">pubs and cafes</a>
and <a href="https://mapcomplete.osm.be/food.html">restaurants</a>),
performance improvements and new features. The post ends with a
request to help develop MapComplete, <em>e.g.</em>, with <a href="https://hosted.weblate.org/projects/mapcomplete/">translation</a>.</li>
<li id="wn586_25691">Bo Percival is <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/bo_hot/diary/397801">seeking</a>
the community’s views on the Tasking Manager’s
‘tomorrow’. HOT_tech are also on the hunt for a
possible community representative product owner for TM, so if this
sounds like something you could be interested in, please get in
touch.</li>
<li id="wn586_25704">Sarah Hoffmann <a href="https://nominatim.org/2021/10/10/detecting-languages.html">discussed</a>
some of the issues encountered when trying to deal with names in
different languages or mixed-lingual names. The next version of
Nominatim will support language-specific handling of names,
including for names that do not have a language suffix.</li>
<li id="wn586_25675">The subway validator (we <a href="https://weeklyosm.eu/archives/14898#wn585_25640">reported</a>
earlier), initially created by Ilya Zverev, is now being <a href="https://maps.mail.ru/osm/tools/subways/latest/">hosted</a> by
Mail.ru. Some details about this tool are <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Quality_assurance#subway-preprocessor">
available</a> on the OSM Wiki and the <a href="https://github.com/alexey-zakharenkov/subways">code</a> is on
GitHub.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_did_you_know_…">Did you know …</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25703">… that the key
<code>floor:material</code> <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Key:floor:material">is
designed</a> for tagging ceilings (technically the lowest part of a
building part with a non-zero <code>minlevel</code>). taginfo
suggests that it is in fact used for tagging floors, at least in
places like <a href="https://taginfo.geofabrik.de/asia/nepal/search?q=floor%3Amaterial">
Nepal</a>. It is one of a number of confusing tag names <a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Counterintuitive_key_names">documented</a>
on the wiki.</li>
<li id="wn586_25679">… that the shapes of non-circular
turning circles (yes, it’s an <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/oxymoron">oxymoron</a>) can be
<a href="https://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Key:turning_circle">described</a>
with the <code>turning_circle</code> key? The recent documentation
of this usage is by Jdcarls2.</li>
<li id="wn586_25705">… the JOSM style <a href="https://josm.openstreetmap.de/wiki/Styles/Coloured_Streets">Coloured
Streets</a> for better address mapping? nickjohnston <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/user/nickjohnston/diary/395216">explains</a>
how it improves address mapping.</li>
<li id="wn586_25701">… the <a href="https://github.com/VROOM-Project/vroom">vroom-project</a> on
GitHub by Julien Coupey, the open source application to solve the
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Travelling_salesman_problem">travelling
salesman problem</a>? Vroom is BSD-licensed, relies on
OpenStreetMap data, and works with OSRM, Openrouteservice, or
Valhalla.</li>
<li id="wn586_25509">… the <a href="https://wambachers-osm.website/Emergency.html">OSM Emergency
Map</a>?</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="wn586_other_“geo”_things">Other
“geo” things</h2>
<ul>
<li id="wn586_25700">The <a href="https://www.openstreetmap.org/#map=8/38.368/-28.422">Azores
Islands</a> may have been <a href="https://www.cmjornal.pt/sociedade/detalhe/detetada-presenca-humana-nos-acores-700-anos-antes-da-chegada-dos-portugueses">
inhabited</a> <img alt="(pt)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/pt.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://www.cmjornal.pt/sociedade/detalhe/detetada-presenca-humana-nos-acores-700-anos-antes-da-chegada-dos-portugueses">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> 700 years earlier than previously thought, <a href="https://www.pnas.org/content/118/41/e2108236118">reveals</a> a new
study developed by an international team of researchers. Until now
the islands were thought to have been discovered by the Portuguese
in the 15<sup>th</sup> century, namely the island of Santa Maria in
1427 and the islands of Corvo and Flores in 1452.</li>
<li id="wn586_25702">Map war: China <a href="https://www.nzz.ch/international/kartenkrieg-china-diktiert-der-welt-mit-karten-seine-grenzen-ld.1634486?reduced=true">
dictates</a> <img alt="(de)" src="https://blog.openstreetmap.de/wp-uploads/2016/12/de.svg" class=" img-responsive"> &gt;
<a href="https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=auto&amp;tl=EN&amp;u=https://www.nzz.ch/international/kartenkrieg-china-diktiert-der-welt-mit-karten-seine-grenzen-ld.1634486?reduced=true">
<img alt="en" src="https://weeklyosm.eu/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/09/en-green.svg" class=" img-responsive">
</a> (paywalled) its borders to the world with maps.</li>
<li id="wn586_25682"><a href="https://digismak.com/terravision-the-story-of-the-pioneering-project-that-rebelled-against-google/">
<em>The Billion Dollar Code</em></a> is a German Netflix miniseries
that covers, among other things, the legal battle over the
allegation that Google Earth software plagiarised the Terravision
system developed by ART+COM.</li>
</ul>

</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://wikiedu.org/blog/2021/10/14/improving-wikipedias-biographies-of-underrepresented-physicists/">Improving Wikipedia’s biographies of underrepresented
physicists</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">15:51, Thursday, 14 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">
            <figure class="wp-caption alignright img-responsive" id="attachment_41261" style="width: 400px;"><img alt="Nick Geiser in front of a white board" class="size-full wp-image-41261 img-responsive" height="300" src="https://wikiedu.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/Nick_Geiser_featured.jpg" width="400">
<figcaption class="wp-caption-text" id="caption-attachment-41261">
Nick Geiser</figcaption>
</figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Like most people, Nick Geiser
uses Wikipedia every day. As a PhD candidate in theoretical physics
at the University of California, Los Angeles, Nick studies string
theory and uses mathematics to solve problems in quantum gravity.
Outside of research, he works with a variety of organizations to
support under-represented minority groups in STEM
fields.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">When he first saw information
about an American Physical Society (APS) Wiki Scientists course,
where participants would learn to edit Wikipedia with instruction
from Wiki Education, Nick was intrigued, but work and other
distractions kept him from applying.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“A few months after that,
I read an article about the course itself and the experiences of
the Wiki Scientists who took it. I then enthusiastically signed up
for the latest iteration of the course and received a scholarship
from the APS to attend,” he says. “I specifically
wanted to learn how to edit Wikipedia and to spend time improving
the biographical pages for minority physicists.”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Nick joined other APS members in
a six-week course over Zoom, led by Wiki Education’s Will
Kent. As a scientific researcher, Nick says he was familiar with
technical writing, but the idea of editing Wikipedia was still
daunting to him.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“The weekly meetings and
homework assignments were a perfect format to learn the particular
skills of editing Wikipedia that I might have never learned on my
own,” he says. “Frankly, Wikipedia is overwhelming, and
Will broke things down so that I could learn the ropes in
manageable steps.”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Following those steps led Nick
to improve the biography of Argentine theoretical physicist</span>
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Virasoro_(physicist)">
<span style="font-weight: 400;">Miguel Ángel
Virasoro</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, whose work
laid the mathematical groundwork for Nick’s field. The
article was a stub, meaning it was comprised of a handful of
sentences but lacked detail.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“I am also Latino, so I
found Virasoro as a fitting first subject for my Wikipedia
journey,” Nick explains. “Through writing this article,
I learned that a prominent Argentine philosopher with the same name
was the father of the physicist Virasoro, but there was no
reference to this connection on English language Wikipedia! I
disambiguated the two Wikipedia pages and added the fact that they
were father and son. I was incredibly surprised that such an
important fact was missing from the two Wikipedia pages, and I was
happy to have added that particular bit of
information.”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Having learned to edit Wikipedia
through this course, Nick plans to keep contributing content. He
loves how focused he becomes when editing Wikipedia — to the
detriment of his other projects, a statement many Wikipedians all
over the world can identify with. In the future, he plans to both
improve biographies of under-represented physicists as well as
regularly editing more technical articles he’s engaging with
as part of his own research.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“Improving the open-access
reservoir of knowledge on Wikipedia will now be part of my regular
work as an academic,” Nick says. “I think all
academics, including physicists, should learn the basics of editing
Wikipedia. We all write academic papers which may be read by only a
few other researchers. Wikipedia articles, however, may be read by
millions of people. Just a few hours of edits can tangibly improve
a primary source of information for much of the
globe.”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">“Moreover, STEM in
particular has real problems of representation, and improving the
biographical articles on Wikipedia for under-represented minority
scientists can help turn the tide,” he adds. “Aspiring
young scientists are influenced by scientists who look like them,
and the biographies of these scientists will not write
themselves.”</span></p>
<p><em>Image credits: <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:2019_UCLA_Powell_Library_rear_1.jpg">
Beyond My Ken</a>, <a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0">CC BY-SA 4.0</a>,
via Wikimedia Commons;&nbsp;<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Theoretical_Physicist_Nick_Geiser_(2020).jpg">Quant
Mechanic</a>, <a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0">CC BY-SA 4.0</a>,
via Wikimedia Commons</em></p>
        </div>
    </div>
</div><div class="card article">
    <div class="card-content">
        <div class="media">
            <div class="media-content has-text-centered">
                <p class="title article-title"><a class="boxh2" href="https://glamwiki.wordpress.com/2021/10/12/this-month-in-glam-september-2021/">This Month in GLAM: September 2021</a></p>
                <div class="tags has-addons level-item">
                    <span class="tag is-rounded">22:34, Tuesday, 12 2021 October UTC</span>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <div class="content article-body">

find out how to participate</li>

France report</a>: Wikidata training in Musée de Grenoble</li>

Italy report</a>: Call for Italian museums, archives and

Kosovo report</a>: Diaspora Edits Wikipedia Campaign</li>
